			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Netherlands</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">This article is about the constituent country. For the sovereign state and constitutional monarchy, see <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Netherlands (disambiguation)">Netherlands (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Not to be confused with the region of <a href="/wiki/Holland" title="Holland">Holland</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> (<i>de Nederlanden</i>).</div>

<span lang="nl">"Ik zal handhaven"</span>&#160;<span class="languageicon" style="font-size:81%;font-weight:normal;">(<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>)</span><br />

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:85%;">
<li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_aaa"><b><a href="#ref_aaa">^</a></b></span> The official motto is in French. The literal translation into English is "I will maintain"; a better translation, however, is "I will hold firm" or "I will uphold" (namely, the integrity and independence of the territory).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (January 2013)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li value="2"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bbb"><b><a href="#ref_bbb">^</a></b></span> <span lang="nl">In 1816 the motto was abbreviated to "<a href="/wiki/God_zij_met_ons" title="God zij met ons">God zij met ons</a>"</span>&#160;<span class="languageicon" style="font-size:81%;font-weight:normal;">(<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>)</span>. (Used on the edges of coins.)</li>
<li value="3"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ccc"><b><a href="#ref_ccc">^</a></b></span> While <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> is the constitutional capital, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> is the seat of the government.</li>
<li value="4"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ddd"><b><a href="#ref_ddd">^</a></b></span> <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">West Frisian</a> has official status in <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a>.<big><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></big> <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Low_Saxon" title="Dutch Low Saxon">Dutch Low Saxon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limburgish_language" title="Limburgish language">Limburgish</a> are recognised as <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">regional languages</a> by the European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages. <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">Papiamento</a> is recognised by the Dutch government in relation to <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> in relation to both <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>.<big><sup id="cite_ref-languages_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-languages-7">[7]</a></sup></big></li>
<li value="5"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_eee"><b><a href="#ref_eee">^</a></b></span> The euro is used in the European part of the Netherlands and replaced the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">Dutch guilder</a> in 2002. The US dollar is used in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a> and replaced the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antillean_guilder" title="Netherlands Antillean guilder">Netherlands Antillean guilder</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li value="6"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_fff"><b><a href="#ref_fff">^</a></b></span> CET and CEST are used in the European Netherlands, and AST is used in the Caribbean Netherlands.</li>
<li value="7"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ggg"><b><a href="#ref_ggg">^</a></b></span> 599 was the country code designated for the now dissolved <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>. The Caribbean Netherlands still use 599–7 (Bonaire), 599–3 (Sint Eustatius) and 599–4 (Saba).</li>
<li value="8"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_hhh"><b><a href="#ref_hhh">^</a></b></span> <a href="/wiki/.nl" title=".nl">.nl</a> is the common internet top level domain name for the Netherlands. The <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as it is shared with other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states. <a href="/wiki/.bq" title=".bq">.bq</a> is designated, but not in use, for the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>.</li>
</ol>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Netherlands</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/En-us-Netherlands.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Netherlands.ogg" title="File:En-us-Netherlands.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="/ð/ 'th' in 'thy'">ð</span><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'">ər</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <span lang="nl"><i>Nederland</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Dutch" title="Help:IPA for Dutch">[ˈneːdərˌlɑnt]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Nl-Nederland.ogg" title="File:Nl-Nederland.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Nl-Nederland.ogg" class="internal" title="Nl-Nederland.ogg">listen</a>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">Frisian</a>: <span lang="fy"><i>Nederlân</i></span>) is the main <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands#Countries" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">constituent country</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>. It is a densely populated country located in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> with <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">three island territories</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[nb 1]</a></sup> The European part of the Netherlands borders <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to the northwest, sharing <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime borders</a> with Belgium, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup><br />
The three largest cities in the Netherlands are <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>. Amsterdam is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_the_Netherlands" title="Capital of the Netherlands">country's capital</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> while The Hague holds the Dutch seat of <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">parliament</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_Netherlands" title="Cabinet of the Netherlands">government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">port of Rotterdam</a> is the world's largest port outside East-Asia, and by far the largest port in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><br />
The name <i><a href="/wiki/Holland" title="Holland">Holland</a></i> is used informally to refer to the whole of the country of the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[nb 2]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Netherlands" literally means "<a href="/wiki/Lower_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower Countries">lower countries</a>", influenced by its low land and flat geography, with only about 50% of its land exceeding one metre <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eupedia_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eupedia-15">[13]</a></sup> Most of the areas below sea level are man-made. Since the late 16th century, large areas (<a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polders</a>) have been <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">reclaimed</a> from the sea and lakes, amounting to nearly 17% of the country's current land mass. With a <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of 412 people per km<sup>2</sup> – 507 (January 2017) if water is excluded – the Netherlands is classified as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">very densely populated country</a>. Only <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> have both a larger population and higher population density. Nevertheless, the Netherlands is the world's second-largest exporter of food and agricultural products, after the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hollandtrade.com_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollandtrade.com-17">[15]</a></sup> This is partly due to the fertility of the soil and the mild climate. The Netherlands was the third country in the world to have an elected <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>, and since 1848 it has been governed as a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, organised as a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>. The Netherlands has a long history of social tolerance and is generally regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> country, having legalised <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_Netherlands" title="Abortion in the Netherlands">abortion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Netherlands" title="Prostitution in the Netherlands">prostitution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia_in_the_Netherlands" title="Euthanasia in the Netherlands">euthanasia</a>, while maintaining a progressive <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">drugs policy</a>. In 2001, it became the world's first country to legalise <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_Netherlands" title="Same-sex marriage in the Netherlands">same-sex marriage</a>.</p>
<p>The Netherlands is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Ten_(economic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Group of Ten (economic)">G-10</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>; as well as being a part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> and the trilateral <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> Union. The country is host to the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons">Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a> and five international courts: the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_Former_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Special_Tribunal_for_Lebanon" title="Special Tribunal for Lebanon">Special Tribunal for Lebanon</a>. The first four are situated in The Hague, as is the EU's criminal intelligence agency <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a> and judicial co-operation agency <a href="/wiki/Eurojust" title="Eurojust">Eurojust</a>. This has led to the city being dubbed "the world's legal capital."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> The country also ranks second highest in the world's 2016 <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a>, as published by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands has a market-based mixed economy, ranking 17th of 177 countries according to the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> It had the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">thirteenth-highest</a> per capita income in the world in 2013 according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>. In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Happiness_Report" title="World Happiness Report">World Happiness Report</a> ranked the Netherlands as the seventh-happiest country in the world, reflecting its high quality of life.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> The Netherlands also ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">second highest</a> in the Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_(terminology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Netherlands (terminology)">Netherlands (terminology)</a></div>
<p>The Netherlands in its entirety is often referred to by the much older designation "<a href="/wiki/Holland" title="Holland">Holland</a>" (meaning <i>holt land</i>, or wood land), though this refers only to <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a>, two of the nation's twelve provinces, formerly a single province and earlier the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">County of Holland</a>. This originally <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> county emerged from the dissolved <a href="/wiki/Frisian_Kingdom" title="Frisian Kingdom">Frisian Kingdom</a> and was – after the decline of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Duchy of Brabant</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">County of Flanders</a> – economically and politically the most important county in the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> region. Because of this importance, and the emphasis on Holland during the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> and later the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Anglo-Dutch Wars</a> in the 16th, 17th and 18th century, Holland served as a <i><a href="/wiki/Pars_pro_toto" title="Pars pro toto">pars pro toto</a></i> for the entire country, and is nowadays considered either incorrect,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> informal,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> or on occasion opprobrious, depending on the context, but is widely used when referring to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">national football team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>The "region" called Low Countries (comprising <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, the Netherlands and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>) and the "country" of the Netherlands have the same <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponymy</a>. Place names with <i>Neder</i> (or <i>lage</i>), <i>Nieder</i>, <i>Nether</i> (or <i>low</i>) and <i>Nedre</i> (in <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a>) and <i>Bas</i> or <i>Inferior</i> (in <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>) are in use in places all over Europe. They are sometimes used in a <a href="/wiki/Deictic" class="mw-redirect" title="Deictic">deictic</a> relation to a higher ground that consecutively is indicated as <i>Upper</i>, <i>Boven</i>, <i>Oben</i>, <i>Superior</i> or <i>Haut</i>. In the case of the Low Countries / the Netherlands the geographical location of the <i>lower</i> region has been more or less downstream and near the sea. The geographical location of the upper region, however, changed over time tremendously. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> made a distinction between the Roman provinces of downstream <a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a> (nowadays part of Belgium and the Netherlands) and upstream <a href="/wiki/Germania_Superior" title="Germania Superior">Germania Superior</a> (nowadays part of Germany). The designation 'Low' to refer to the region returns again in the 10th century Duchy of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Lorraine" title="Lower Lorraine">Lower Lorraine</a>, that covered much of the Low Countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Franks_.28Columbia_Encyclopedia.29_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Franks_.28Columbia_Encyclopedia.29-26">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> But this time the corresponding <i>Upper</i> region is <a href="/wiki/Upper_Lorraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Lorraine">Upper Lorraine</a>, in nowadays Northern France.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dukes_of_Burgundy" class="mw-redirect" title="Dukes of Burgundy">Dukes of Burgundy</a>, who ruled the Low Countries in the 15th century, used the term <i>les pays de par deçà</i> (~ the lands over here) for the Low Countries as opposed to <i>les pays de par delà</i> (~ the lands over there) for their original homeland: <a href="/wiki/Burgundy" title="Burgundy">Burgundy</a> in present-day east-central France.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Netherlands" title="Habsburg Netherlands">Habsburg rule</a>, <i>Les pays de par deçà</i> developed in <i>pays d'embas</i> (lands down-here),<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> a deictic expression in relation to other Habsburg possessions in Europe. This was translated as <i>Neder-landen</i> in contemporary Dutch official documents.<sup id="cite_ref-Lem_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lem-30">[28]</a></sup> From a regional point of view, <i>Niderlant</i> was also the area between the <a href="/wiki/Meuse_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Meuse (river)">Meuse</a> and the lower <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> in the late Middle Ages. The area known as <i>Oberland</i> (High country) was in this deictic context considered to begin approximately at the nearby higher located <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>.</p>
<p>From the mid-sixteenth century on, "the Low Countries" and "the Netherlands" lost their original deictic meaning, and were&#160;– besides <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>&#160;– probably the most commonly used names. The <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> (1568–1648) divided the Low Countries into an independent northern <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Latinisation_of_names" title="Latinisation of names">Latinised</a> <i>Belgica Foederata</i>, "Federated Netherlands", the precursor state of the Netherlands) and a Spanish controlled <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a> (Latinised <i>Belgica Regia</i>, "Royal Netherlands", the precursor state of Belgium). The Low Countries today is a designation that includes the countries the Netherlands, Belgium and Luxembourg, although in most <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>, the term "Low Countries" is used as the name for the Netherlands specifically. It is used synonymous with the more neutral and geopolitical term <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Netherlands">History of the Netherlands</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_.28before_500_BC.29">Prehistory (before 500 BC)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory (before 500 BC)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:5500vc_ex_leg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/5500vc_ex_leg.jpg/170px-5500vc_ex_leg.jpg" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/5500vc_ex_leg.jpg/255px-5500vc_ex_leg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/5500vc_ex_leg.jpg/340px-5500vc_ex_leg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="510" data-file-height="616" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg/170px-500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg/255px-500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg/340px-500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="510" data-file-height="616" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:500vc_ex_leg_copy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Netherlands in 500 BC</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg/130px-Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg" width="130" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg/195px-Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg/260px-Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="1280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An oak figurine found in <a href="/wiki/Willemstad,_North_Brabant" title="Willemstad, North Brabant">Willemstad, North Brabant</a> (4500 BC)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The prehistory of the area that is now the Netherlands was largely shaped by the sea and the rivers that constantly shifted the low-lying geography. The oldest human (<a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a>) traces in the Netherlands were found in higher soils, near <a href="/wiki/Maastricht" title="Maastricht">Maastricht</a>, from what is believed to be about 250,000 years ago. After the end of the Ice Age, various <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> groups inhabited the area, and around 8000 BC <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> tribes resided in Friesland and Drenthe, where the <a href="/wiki/Pesse_canoe" title="Pesse canoe">oldest canoe</a> in the world was recovered.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> Autochthonous <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherers" class="mw-redirect" title="Hunter-gatherers">hunter-gatherers</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Swifterbant_culture" title="Swifterbant culture">Swifterbant culture</a> are attested from around 5600 BC onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-Kooijmans1998_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kooijmans1998-32">[30]</a></sup> They are strongly linked to rivers and open water and were related to the southern Scandinavian <a href="/wiki/Erteb%C3%B8lle_culture" title="Ertebølle culture">Ertebølle culture</a> (5300–4000 BC). To the west, the same tribes might have built hunting camps to hunt winter game. People made the switch to <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a> sometime between 4800 BC and 4500 BC. Agricultural transformation took place very gradually, between 4300 BC and 4000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> The farming <a href="/wiki/Funnelbeaker_culture" title="Funnelbeaker culture">Funnelbeaker culture</a> extended from Denmark through northern Germany into the northern Netherlands, and erected the <a href="/wiki/Dolmens" class="mw-redirect" title="Dolmens">dolmens</a>, large stone grave monuments found in <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a> (built between 4100 BC and 3200 BC). To the southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Vlaardingen_culture" title="Vlaardingen culture">Vlaardingen culture</a> (around 2600 BC), an apparently more primitive culture of hunter-gatherers survived well into the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period. Around 2950 BC there was a quick and smooth transition from the <a href="/wiki/Funnelbeaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Funnelbeaker">Funnelbeaker</a> farming culture to the pan-European <a href="/wiki/Corded_Ware" class="mw-redirect" title="Corded Ware">Corded Ware</a> pastoralist culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloemers_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloemers-34">[32]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bell_Beaker_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell Beaker culture">Bell Beaker culture</a>, also present in the Netherlands, apparently rose out of the Corded Ware culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Lanting_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lanting-35">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Discoveries of copper artifacts imply trade with other parts of Europe, as the metal is not normally found in Dutch soil. The <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> probably started somewhere around 2000 BC and lasted until around 800 BC. The many finds in <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a> of rare and valuable objects, suggest that it was a trading centre in the Bronze Age. The <a href="/wiki/Beaker_culture" title="Beaker culture">Bell Beaker cultures</a> (2700–2100 BC) locally developed into the Bronze Age Barbed-Wire Beaker culture (2100–1800 BC). In the second millennium BC, the region was the boundary between the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Bronze_Age" title="Atlantic Bronze Age">Atlantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Bronze_Age" title="Nordic Bronze Age">Nordic</a> horizons, roughly divided by the course of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>. In the north, the <a href="/wiki/Elp_culture" title="Elp culture">Elp culture</a> (c. 1800 BC to 800 BC)<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> was a <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> archaeological culture having <a href="/wiki/Earthenware" title="Earthenware">earthenware</a> pottery of low quality as a marker. The initial phase was characterised by <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">tumuli</a> (1800–1200 BC) that were strongly tied to contemporary tumuli in northern Germany and Scandinavia, and were apparently related to the <a href="/wiki/Tumulus_culture" title="Tumulus culture">Tumulus culture</a> (1600–1200 BC) in central Europe. This phase was followed by a subsequent change featuring <a href="/wiki/Urnfield" class="mw-redirect" title="Urnfield">Urnfield</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cremation" title="Cremation">cremation</a>) burial customs (1200–800 BC). The southern region became dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Hilversum_culture" title="Hilversum culture">Hilversum culture</a> (1800–800 BC), which apparently inherited cultural ties with Britain of the previous Barbed-Wire Beaker culture.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> brought a measure of prosperity. Iron ore was available throughout the country, including <a href="/wiki/Bog_iron" title="Bog iron">bog iron</a> extracted from the <a href="/wiki/Ore" title="Ore">ore</a> in <a href="/wiki/Peat_bogs" class="mw-redirect" title="Peat bogs">peat bogs</a> in the north, the natural iron-bearing balls found in the <a href="/wiki/Veluwe" title="Veluwe">Veluwe</a> and the red iron ore near the rivers in Brabant. <a href="/wiki/Blacksmith" title="Blacksmith">Smiths</a> travelled from small settlement to settlement with <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> and iron, fabricating tools on demand, including <a href="/wiki/Axe" title="Axe">axes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knife" title="Knife">knives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pins" class="mw-redirect" title="Pins">pins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrowheads" class="mw-redirect" title="Arrowheads">arrowheads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sword" title="Sword">swords</a>. Some evidence even suggests the making of <a href="/wiki/Damascus_steel" title="Damascus steel">Damascus steel</a> <a href="/wiki/Sword" title="Sword">swords</a> using an advanced method of <a href="/wiki/Forging" title="Forging">forging</a> that combined the flexibility of iron with the strength of steel. The <a href="/wiki/Vorstengraf_(Oss)" title="Vorstengraf (Oss)">King's grave of Oss</a> dating from around 500 BC was found in a burial mound, the largest of its kind in western Europe and containing an iron sword with an inlay of gold and coral.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germanic_groups_and_Romans_.28500_BC_.E2.80.93_410_AD.29">Germanic groups and Romans (500 BC – 410 AD)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Germanic groups and Romans (500 BC – 410 AD)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romans_in_the_Netherlands" title="Romans in the Netherlands">Romans in the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png/170px-Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png" width="170" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png/255px-Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png/340px-Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png 2x" data-file-width="419" data-file-height="431" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Germanic_dialects_ca._AD_1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Germanic dialects around 1 AD
<div class="legend"><small><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_languages" title="North Germanic languages">North Germanic</a></small></div>
<div class="legend"><small><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="North Sea Germanic">North Sea Germanic</a></small></div>
<div class="legend"><small><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Weser-Rhine_Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Weser-Rhine Germanic">Weser-Rhine Germanic</a></small></div>
<div class="legend"><small><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Elbe_Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Elbe Germanic">Elbe Germanic</a></small></div>
<div class="legend"><small><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/East_Germanic_languages" title="East Germanic languages">East Germanic</a></small></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png/220px-Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png/330px-Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png/440px-Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="314" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF43; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Diachronic_linguistics" class="mw-redirect" title="Diachronic linguistics">Diachronic</a> distribution of Celtic peoples from 500 BC</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #97FFB6; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;expansion into the southern Low Countries by 270 BC</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The deteriorating climate in Scandinavia around 850 BC, that further deteriorated around 650 BC, might have triggered migration of <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> tribes from the North. By the time this migration was complete, around 250 BC, a few general cultural and linguistic groups had emerged.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Verhaal_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-39">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="North Sea Germanic">North Sea Germanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Ingvaeones" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingvaeones">Ingvaeones</a> inhabited the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>. They would later develop into the <a href="/wiki/Frisii" title="Frisii">Frisii</a> and the early <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Verhaal_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-39">[37]</a></sup> A second grouping, the <a href="/wiki/Weser-Rhine_Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Weser-Rhine Germanic">Weser-Rhine Germanic</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Istvaeones" title="Istvaeones">Istvaeones</a>), extended along the middle Rhine and <a href="/wiki/Weser" title="Weser">Weser</a> and inhabited the Low Countries south of the great rivers. This group consisted of tribes that would eventually develop into the <a href="/wiki/Salian_Franks" title="Salian Franks">Salian Franks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Verhaal_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-39">[37]</a></sup> Also the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/La_T%C3%A8ne_culture" title="La Tène culture">La Tène culture</a> (c. 450 BC up to the Roman conquest) had expanded over a wide range, including the southern area of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>. Some scholars have speculated that even a third ethnic identity and language, neither Germanic nor Celtic, survived in the Netherlands until the Roman period, the Iron Age <a href="/wiki/Nordwestblock" title="Nordwestblock">Nordwestblock</a> culture,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lendering_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lendering-41">[39]</a></sup> that eventually was being absorbed by the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> to the south and the Germanic peoples from the east.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Germania_70.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Germania_70.svg/220px-Germania_70.svg.png" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Germania_70.svg/330px-Germania_70.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Germania_70.svg/440px-Germania_70.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="972" data-file-height="780" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Germania_70.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rhine Frontier of around 70 AD</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Gallic_Wars" title="Gallic Wars">Gallic Wars</a>, the area south of the <a href="/wiki/Oude_Rijn_(Utrecht_and_South_Holland)" title="Oude Rijn (Utrecht and South Holland)">Oude Rijn</a> and west of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman forces</a> under <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> from 57 BC to 53 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Lendering_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lendering-41">[39]</a></sup> Caesar describes two main tribes living in what is now the southern Netherlands: the <a href="/wiki/Menapii" title="Menapii">Menapii</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eburones" title="Eburones">Eburones</a>. The Rhine became fixed as Rome's northern frontier around 12 AD. Notable towns would arise along the <a href="/wiki/Limes_Germanicus" title="Limes Germanicus">Limes Germanicus</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen" title="Nijmegen">Nijmegen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voorburg" title="Voorburg">Voorburg</a>. At first part of <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Belgica" title="Gallia Belgica">Gallia Belgica</a>, the area south of the Limes became part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a>. The area to the north of the Rhine, inhabited by the Frisii, remained outside Roman rule (but not its presence and control), while the border tribes <a href="/wiki/Batavi_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Batavi (Germanic tribe)">Batavi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cananefates" title="Cananefates">Cananefates</a> served in the <a href="/wiki/Ala_(Roman_military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ala (Roman military)">Roman cavalry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> The Batavi rose against the Romans in the <a href="/wiki/Batavian_rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Batavian rebellion">Batavian rebellion</a> of 69AD, but were eventually defeated. The Batavi later merged with other tribes into the confederation of the <a href="/wiki/Salian_Franks" title="Salian Franks">Salian Franks</a>, whose identity emerged at the first half of the third century.<sup id="cite_ref-Previt.C3.A9-Orton_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Previt.C3.A9-Orton-43">[41]</a></sup> Salian Franks appear in Roman texts as both allies and enemies. The Salian Franks were forced by the confederation of the <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a> from the east to move over the Rhine into Roman territory in the fourth century. From their new base in West Flanders and the Southwest Netherlands, they were raiding the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>. Roman forces pacified the region, but did not expel the Franks, who continued to be feared at least until the time of <a href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian the Apostate">Julian the Apostate</a> (358), when Salian Franks were allowed to settle as <i><a href="/wiki/Foederati" title="Foederati">foederati</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Toxandria" class="mw-redirect" title="Toxandria">Toxandria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Previt.C3.A9-Orton_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Previt.C3.A9-Orton-43">[41]</a></sup> After deteriorating climate conditions and the Romans withdrawal, the <a href="/wiki/Frisii" title="Frisii">Frisii</a> disappeared from the northern Netherlands, probably forced to resettle within Roman territory as <i><a href="/wiki/Laeti" title="Laeti">laeti</a></i> in c. 296. Coastal lands remained largely unpopulated for the next two centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Middle_Ages_.28411.E2.80.931000.29">Early Middle Ages (411–1000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early Middle Ages (411–1000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Frankish_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish Kingdom">Frankish Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frisian_Kingdom" title="Frisian Kingdom">Frisian Kingdom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frisia_716-la.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Frisia_716-la.svg/170px-Frisia_716-la.svg.png" width="170" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Frisia_716-la.svg/255px-Frisia_716-la.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Frisia_716-la.svg/340px-Frisia_716-la.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="583" data-file-height="602" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frisia_716-la.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Franks, Frisians and Saxons (c. 716 AD)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> government in the area collapsed, the Franks expanded their territories in numerous kingdoms. By the 490s, <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">Clovis I</a> had conquered and united all these territories in the southern Netherlands in one <a href="/wiki/Frankish_kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish kingdom">Frankish kingdom</a>, and from there continued his conquests into <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>. During this expansion, Franks migrating to the south eventually adopted the <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> of the local population.<sup id="cite_ref-Verhaal_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-39">[37]</a></sup> A widening cultural divide grew with the Franks remaining in their original homeland in the north (i.e. southern Netherlands and Flanders), who kept on speaking <a href="/wiki/Old_Frankish" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Frankish">Old Frankish</a>, which by the ninth century had evolved into <a href="/wiki/Old_Low_Franconian" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Low Franconian">Old Low Franconian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Old_Dutch" title="Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Verhaal_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-39">[37]</a></sup> A Dutch-French language boundary came into existence.<sup id="cite_ref-Verhaal_39-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-39">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franks_expansion.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franks_expansion.gif/170px-Franks_expansion.gif" width="170" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franks_expansion.gif/255px-Franks_expansion.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franks_expansion.gif/340px-Franks_expansion.gif 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="505" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franks_expansion.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Frankish expansion (481 to 870 AD)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To the north of the Franks, climatic conditions on the coast improved, and during the <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">Migration Period</a> the abandoned land was resettled again, mostly by <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>, but also by the closely related <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jutes" title="Jutes">Jutes</a> and ancient <a href="/wiki/Frisii" title="Frisii">Frisii</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity-46">[44]</a></sup> Many moved on to <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and came to be known as <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a>, but those who stayed would be referred to as <a href="/wiki/Frisians" title="Frisians">Frisians</a> and their language as <a href="/wiki/Frisian_languages" title="Frisian languages">Frisian</a>, named after the land that was once inhabited by Frisii.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity-46">[44]</a></sup> Frisian was spoken along the entire southern North Sea coast, and it is still the language most closely related to English among the living languages of continental Europe. By the seventh century a <a href="/wiki/Frisian_Kingdom" title="Frisian Kingdom">Frisian Kingdom</a> (650–734) under King <a href="/wiki/Aldegisel" class="mw-redirect" title="Aldegisel">Aldegisel</a> and King <a href="/wiki/Redbad,_King_of_the_Frisians" title="Redbad, King of the Frisians">Redbad</a> emerged with <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Utrecht (city)">Utrecht</a> as its centre of power,<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity-46">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Dorestad" title="Dorestad">Dorestad</a> was a flourishing trading place.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Atlas_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atlas-49">[47]</a></sup> Between 600 and around 719 the cities were often fought over between the Frisians and the Franks. In 734, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Boarn" title="Battle of the Boarn">Battle of the Boarn</a>, the Frisians were defeated after a <a href="/wiki/Frisian%E2%80%93Frankish_wars" title="Frisian–Frankish wars">series of wars</a>. With the approval of the Franks, the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_mission" title="Anglo-Saxon mission">Anglo-Saxon</a> missionary <a href="/wiki/Willibrord" title="Willibrord">Willibrord</a> converted the Frisian people to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. He established the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Utrecht_(695%E2%80%931580)" title="Archdiocese of Utrecht (695–1580)">Archdiocese of Utrecht</a> and became bishop of the Frisians. However, his successor Boniface was murdered by the Frisians in <a href="/wiki/Dokkum" title="Dokkum">Dokkum</a>, in 754.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:800nc_ex_leg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/800nc_ex_leg.jpg/170px-800nc_ex_leg.jpg" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/800nc_ex_leg.jpg/255px-800nc_ex_leg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/800nc_ex_leg.jpg/340px-800nc_ex_leg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="510" data-file-height="613" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:800nc_ex_leg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Geography of the Netherlands c. 800AD</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg/170px-Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg/255px-Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg/340px-Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="843" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rorik_of_Dorestad" title="Rorik of Dorestad">Rorik of Dorestad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> ruler of <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a> (romantic 1912 depiction)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Frankish <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Carolingian empire">Carolingian empire</a> modeled itself after the Roman Empire and controlled much of Western Europe. However, as of 843, it was divided into three parts—<a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Francia" title="Middle Francia">Middle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Francia" title="West Francia">West Francia</a>. Most of present-day Netherlands became part of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Francia" title="Middle Francia">Middle Francia</a>, which was a weak kingdom and subject of numerous partitions and annexation attempts by its stronger neighbours. It comprises territories from <a href="/wiki/Frisia" title="Frisia">Frisia</a> in the north to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(medieval)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Italy (medieval)">Kingdom of Italy</a> in the south. When the middle kingdom was partitioned, the lands north of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> passed to <a href="/wiki/Lothair_II_of_Lotharingia" class="mw-redirect" title="Lothair II of Lotharingia">Lothair II</a> and consecutively were named <a href="/wiki/Lotharingia" title="Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>. After he died in 869, Lotharingia was partitioned, into <a href="/wiki/Upper_Lotharingia" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Lotharingia">Upper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Lotharingia" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower Lotharingia">Lower Lotharingia</a>, the latter part comprising the Low Countries that technically became part of <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a> in 870, although it was effectively under the control of Vikings, who raided the largely defenceless <a href="/wiki/Frisians" title="Frisians">Frisian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> towns lying on the Frisian coast and along the rivers. Around 850, <a href="/wiki/Lothair_I" title="Lothair I">Lothair I</a> acknowledged the Viking <a href="/wiki/Rorik_of_Dorestad" title="Rorik of Dorestad">Rorik of Dorestad</a> as ruler of most of Frisia.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> Around 879, another Viking raided the Frisian lands, <a href="/wiki/Godfrid,_Duke_of_Frisia" title="Godfrid, Duke of Frisia">Godfrid, Duke of Frisia</a>. The Viking raids made the sway of French and German lords in the area weak. Resistance to the Vikings, if any, came from local nobles, who gained in stature as a result, and that lay the basis for the disintegration of Lower Lotharingia into semi-independent states. One of these local nobles was <a href="/wiki/Gerolf_of_Holland" title="Gerolf of Holland">Gerolf of Holland</a>, who assumed lordship in Frisia after he helped to assassinate Godfrid, and Viking rule came to an end.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Middle_Ages_.281000.E2.80.931384.29">High Middle Ages (1000–1384)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: High Middle Ages (1000–1384)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_urban_centers_in_the_Low_Countries" title="History of urban centers in the Low Countries">History of urban centers in the Low Countries</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> (the successor state of East Francia) ruled much of the Low Countries in the 10th and 11th century, but was not able to maintain political unity. Powerful local nobles turned their cities, counties and duchies into private kingdoms, that felt little sense of obligation to the emperor. <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Hainaut" title="County of Hainaut">Hainaut</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Gelre" class="mw-redirect" title="Duchy of Gelre">Gelre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Brabant</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishopric of Utrecht">Utrecht</a> were in a state of almost continual war or paradoxically formed personal unions. The language and culture of most of the people who lived in the County of Holland were originally <a href="/wiki/Frisia" title="Frisia">Frisian</a>. As Frankish settlement progressed from Flanders and Brabant, the area quickly became <a href="/wiki/Old_Low_Franconian" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Low Franconian">Old Low Franconian</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Old_Dutch" title="Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a>). The rest of <a href="/wiki/Frisia" title="Frisia">Frisia</a> in the north (now <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Groningen_(province)" title="Groningen (province)">Groningen</a>) continued to maintain its independence and had its own institutions (collectively called the "<a href="/wiki/Frisian_freedom" title="Frisian freedom">Frisian freedom</a>") and resented the imposition of the feudal system.</p>
<p>Around 1000 AD, due to several agricultural developments, the economy started to develop at a fast pace, and the higher productivity allowed workers to farm more land or to become tradesmen. Towns grew around <a href="/wiki/Monasteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Monasteries">monasteries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castles" class="mw-redirect" title="Castles">castles</a>, and a mercantile middle class began to develop in these urban areas, especially in Flanders and later also Brabant. Wealthy cities started to buy certain <a href="/wiki/City_rights_in_the_Low_Countries" title="City rights in the Low Countries">privileges</a> for themselves from the <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">sovereign</a>. In practice, this meant that <a href="/wiki/Brugge" class="mw-redirect" title="Brugge">Brugge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> became quasi-independent republics in their own right and would later develop into some of the most important cities and ports in Europe.</p>
<p>Around 1100 AD, farmers from <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishopric of Utrecht">Utrecht</a> began draining and cultivating uninhabited swampy land in the western Netherlands, and made the emergence of the County of Holland as center of power possible. The title of <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Holland" title="Count of Holland">Count of Holland</a> were fought over in the <a href="/wiki/Hook_and_Cod_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Hook and Cod Wars">Hook and Cod Wars</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <span lang="nl"><i>Hoekse en Kabeljauwse twisten</i></span>) between 1350 and 1490. The Cod faction consisted of the more progressive cities, while the Hook faction consisted of the conservative noblemen. These noblemen invited the Duke <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Good" title="Philip the Good">Philip the Good</a> of Burgundy – who was also Count of Flanders – to conquer Holland.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burgundian_and_Habsburg_Netherlands_.281384.E2.80.931581.29">Burgundian and Habsburg Netherlands (1384–1581)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Burgundian and Habsburg Netherlands (1384–1581)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Netherlands" title="Burgundian Netherlands">Burgundian Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Netherlands" title="Habsburg Netherlands">Habsburg Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Van_Soest,_Four_Days_Battle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg/220px-Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg/330px-Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg/440px-Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="516" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Van_Soest,_Four_Days_Battle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The <a href="/wiki/Four_Days%27_Battle" title="Four Days' Battle">Four Days' Battle</a>, 1–4 June 1666</i>, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo%E2%80%93Dutch_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Anglo–Dutch War">Second Anglo–Dutch War</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_(1350)-NL.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg/170px-Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg.png" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg/255px-Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg/340px-Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2818" data-file-height="3608" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_(1350)-NL.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Low Countries in the late 14th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Imperial</a> and <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="France in the Middle Ages">French</a> fiefs in what is now the Netherlands and Belgium were united in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> by Philip the Good, duke of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Burgundy" title="Duchy of Burgundy">Burgundy</a> in 1433. The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Valois-Burgundy" title="House of Valois-Burgundy">House of Valois-Burgundy</a> and their <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> heirs would rule the Low Countries in the period from 1384 to 1581. Before the Burgundian union, the Dutch identified themselves by the town they lived in or their local duchy or county. The Burgundian period is when the road to nationhood began. The new rulers defended Dutch trading interests, which then developed rapidly. The fleets of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">County of Holland</a> defeated the fleets of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> several times. <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> grew and in the 15th century became the primary trading port in Europe for grain from the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">Baltic region</a>. Amsterdam distributed grain to the major cities of Belgium, Northern France and England. This trade was vital, because Holland could no longer produce enough grain to feed itself. Land drainage had caused the <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> of the former <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> to reduce to a level that was too low for drainage to be maintained.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_I,_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg/170px-William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg/255px-William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg/340px-William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4876" data-file-height="6728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_I,_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
William I, Prince of Orange (<a href="/wiki/William_the_Silent" title="William the Silent">William the Silent</a>), leader of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under Habsburg <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and King of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a>, all fiefs in the current Netherlands region were united into the <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_Provinces" title="Seventeen Provinces">Seventeen Provinces</a>, which also included most of present-day <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, Luxembourg, and some adjacent land in what is now France and Germany. In 1568, the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> between the Provinces and their <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> ruler began. In 1579, the northern half of the Seventeen Provinces forged the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Utrecht" title="Union of Utrecht">Union of Utrecht</a> in which they committed to support each other in their defence against the Spanish army.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> The Union of Utrecht is seen as the foundation of the modern Netherlands. In 1581, the northern provinces adopted the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Abjuration" title="Act of Abjuration">Act of Abjuration</a>, the declaration of independence in which the provinces officially deposed <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> as reigning monarch in the northern provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a> sympathised with the Dutch struggle against the Spanish, and sent an army of 7,600 soldiers to aid the Dutch in their war with the Catholic Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> The English army under command of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Dudley,_1st_Earl_of_Leicester" title="Robert Dudley, 1st Earl of Leicester">Robert Dudley, 1st Earl of Leicester</a> was of no real benefit to the Dutch rebellion.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> Philip II, the son of Charles V, was not prepared to let them go easily, and war continued until 1648, when Spain under King <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">Philip IV</a> finally recognised the independence of the seven north-western provinces in the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster" title="Peace of Münster">Peace of Münster</a>. Parts of the southern provinces became <i>de facto</i> colonies of the new republican-mercantile empire.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_Republic_.281581.E2.80.931795.29">Dutch Republic (1581–1795)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dutch Republic (1581–1795)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_Dutch_Empire" title="Evolution of the Dutch Empire">Evolution of the Dutch Empire</a></div>
<p>After declaring their independence, the provinces of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Zeeland" title="County of Zeeland">Zeeland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Groningen" title="Lordship of Groningen">Groningen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Friesland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lordship of Friesland">Friesland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Utrecht" title="Lordship of Utrecht">Utrecht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Overijssel" title="Lordship of Overijssel">Overijssel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Gelderland" class="mw-redirect" title="Duchy of Gelderland">Gelderland</a> formed a <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a>. All these duchies, lordships and counties were autonomous and had their own government, the <a href="/wiki/States-Provincial" title="States-Provincial">States-Provincial</a>. The <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General</a>, the confederal government, were seated in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> and consisted of representatives from each of the seven provinces. The sparsely populated region of <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Drenthe" class="mw-redirect" title="Lordship of Drenthe">Drenthe</a> was part of the republic too, although it was not considered one of the provinces. Moreover, the Republic had come to occupy during the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> a number of so-called <a href="/wiki/Generality_Lands" title="Generality Lands">Generality Lands</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Brabant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Limburg" title="Duchy of Limburg">Limburg</a>. Their population was mainly Roman Catholic, and these areas did not have a governmental structure of their own, and were used as a buffer zone between the Republic and the Spanish-controlled <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg/220px-Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg/330px-Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg/440px-Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2303" data-file-height="1232" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Winter landscape with skaters c. 1625</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg/220px-Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg/330px-Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg/440px-Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2505" data-file-height="1475" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a> in 1656</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>, spanning much of the 17th century, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a> grew to become one of the major seafaring and economic powers. Science, military, and art (especially <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age_painting" title="Dutch Golden Age painting">painting</a>) were among the most acclaimed in the world. By 1650, the Dutch owned 16,000 merchant ships.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> established <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> all over the world, including ruling the northern parts of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> between <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Dutch_rule" class="mw-redirect" title="Taiwan under Dutch rule">1624–1662 and 1664–1667</a>. The <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">Dutch settlement in North America</a> began with the founding of <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> on the southern part of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> in 1614. In South Africa, the Dutch settled the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a> in 1652. <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonisation_of_the_Guianas" title="Dutch colonisation of the Guianas">Dutch colonies in South America</a> were established along the many rivers in the fertile <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> plains, among them <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Colony of Surinam</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>). In Asia, the Dutch established the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>), and the only western trading post in Japan, <a href="/wiki/Dejima" title="Dejima">Dejima</a>.</p>
<p>Many economic historians regard the Netherlands as the first thoroughly <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> country in the world. In early modern Europe it had the wealthiest trading city (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>) and the first full-time <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">stock exchange</a>. The inventiveness of the traders led to insurance and retirement funds as well as phenomena such as the <a href="/wiki/Boom_and_bust" class="mw-redirect" title="Boom and bust">boom-bust cycle</a>, the world's first <a href="/wiki/Asset_price_inflation" title="Asset price inflation">asset-inflation bubble</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tulip_mania" title="Tulip mania">tulip mania</a> of 1636–1637, and the world's first <a href="/wiki/Bear_raid" title="Bear raid">bear raider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_le_Maire" class="mw-redirect" title="Isaac le Maire">Isaac le Maire</a>, who forced prices down by dumping stock and then buying it back at a discount.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> In 1672 – known in Dutch history as the <a href="/wiki/Rampjaar" title="Rampjaar">Rampjaar</a> (Disaster Year) – the Dutch Republic was in war with France, England and three German Bishoprics simultaneously. At sea it could successfully prevent the English and French navy entering the western shores. On land, however, it was almost taken over interlay by the advancing French and German armies coming from the east.
