It could however turn the tide by <a href="/wiki/Hollandic_Water_Line" title="Hollandic Water Line">inundating parts of Holland</a>, but could never recover to its former glory again and went into a state of general decline in the 18th century, with economic competition from England and long-standing rivalries between the two main factions in Dutch society, the republican <a href="/wiki/Dutch_States_Party" title="Dutch States Party"><i>Staatsgezinden</i></a> and the supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Stadtholder" title="Stadtholder">stadtholder</a> the <a href="/wiki/Orangism_(Netherlands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orangism (Netherlands)"><i>Prinsgezinden</i></a>, as main <a href="/wiki/Political_faction" title="Political faction">political factions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Batavian_Republic_and_kingdom_.281795.E2.80.931890.29">Batavian Republic and kingdom (1795–1890)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Batavian Republic and kingdom (1795–1890)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Batavian Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Holland" title="Kingdom of Holland">Kingdom of Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>With the armed support of <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">revolutionary France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patriots_(faction)" class="mw-redirect" title="Patriots (faction)">Dutch republicans</a> proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Batavian Republic</a>, modelled after the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">French Republic</a> and rendering the Netherlands a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> on 19 January 1795. The <a href="/wiki/Stadtholder" title="Stadtholder">stadtholder</a> <a href="/wiki/William_V_of_Orange" class="mw-redirect" title="William V of Orange">William V of Orange</a> had fled to England. But from 1806 to 1810, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Holland" title="Kingdom of Holland">Kingdom of Holland</a> was set up by <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> as a puppet kingdom governed by his brother <a href="/wiki/Louis_Bonaparte" title="Louis Bonaparte">Louis Bonaparte</a> to control the Netherlands more effectively. However, King Louis Bonaparte tried to serve Dutch interests instead of his brother's, and he was forced to abdicate on 1 July 1810. The Emperor sent in an army and the Netherlands became part of the French Empire until the autumn of 1813, when Napoleon was defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">Battle of Leipzig</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_Empire35.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Dutch_Empire35.PNG/220px-Dutch_Empire35.PNG" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Dutch_Empire35.PNG/330px-Dutch_Empire35.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Dutch_Empire35.PNG/440px-Dutch_Empire35.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1678" data-file-height="893" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_Empire35.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch colonial empire</a>. Light green: territories administered by or originating from territories administered by the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>; dark green: the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a>. In yellow the territories occupied later, during the 19th century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_I_of_the_Netherlands" title="William I of the Netherlands">William Frederick</a>, son of the last stadtholder, returned to the Netherlands in 1813 and proclaimed himself <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Principality_of_the_United_Netherlands" title="Sovereign Principality of the United Netherlands">Sovereign Prince of the Netherlands</a>. Two years later, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> added the southern Netherlands to the north to create a strong country on the northern border of France. William Frederick raised this <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Netherlands</a> to the status of a kingdom and proclaimed himself <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_the_Netherlands" title="William I of the Netherlands">King William I</a>. In addition, William became hereditary <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ducal_Family_of_Luxembourg" title="Grand Ducal Family of Luxembourg">Grand Duke of Luxembourg</a> in exchange for his German possessions. However, the Southern Netherlands had been culturally separate from the north since 1581, and <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">rebelled</a>. The south gained independence in 1830 as <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> between Luxembourg and the Netherlands was severed in 1890, when <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_the_Netherlands" title="William III of the Netherlands">William III</a> died with no surviving male heirs. <a href="/wiki/Salic_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Salic Law">Ascendancy laws</a> prevented his daughter <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmina_of_the_Netherlands" title="Wilhelmina of the Netherlands">Queen Wilhelmina</a> from becoming the next Grand Duchess.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/220px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/330px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/440px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6124" data-file-height="4608" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The submission of <a href="/wiki/Diponegoro" title="Diponegoro">Diponegoro</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Merkus_de_Kock" title="Hendrik Merkus de Kock">General De Kock</a> at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Java_War" title="Java War">Java War</a> in 1830; <a href="/wiki/The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock" title="The Submission of Prince Dipo Negoro to General De Kock">painting</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nicolaas_Pieneman" title="Nicolaas Pieneman">Nicolaas Pieneman</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Belgian Revolution at home and the <a href="/wiki/Java_War" title="Java War">Java War</a> in the Dutch East Indies brought the Netherlands to the brink of bankruptcy. However, the <a href="/wiki/Cultivation_System" title="Cultivation System">Cultivation System</a> was introduced in 1830; in the Dutch East Indies, 20% of village land had to be devoted to government crops for export. The policy brought the Dutch enormous wealth and made the colony self-sufficient. On the other hand, the colonies in the West Indies (<a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Dutch Guiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Curaçao and Dependencies">Curaçao and Dependencies</a>), relied heavily on <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> in which the Dutch part is estimated at 5–7 percent, or more than half a million Africans. The Netherlands abolished slavery in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> Furthermore, slaves in <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> would be fully free only in 1873, since the law stipulated that there was to be a mandatory 10-year transition.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> The Dutch were also one of the last European countries to <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">industrialise</a>, in the second half of the 19th century.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_wars_and_beyond_.281890.E2.80.93present.29">World wars and beyond (1890–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: World wars and beyond (1890–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands_(1900%E2%80%93present)" title="History of the Netherlands (1900–present)">History of the Netherlands (1900–present)</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Netherlands_in_World_War_I" title="The Netherlands in World War I">The Netherlands in World War I</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_in_World_War_II" title="Netherlands in World War II">Netherlands in World War II</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rotterdam,_Laurenskerk,_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg/220px-Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg/330px-Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg/440px-Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2269" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rotterdam,_Laurenskerk,_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> after <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam_Blitz" title="Rotterdam Blitz">German air raids</a> in 1940.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands were able to remain neutral during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, in part because the import of goods through the Netherlands proved essential to German survival, until the blockade by the British Royal Navy in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-Abbenhuis_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abbenhuis-60">[58]</a></sup> That changed in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Netherlands" title="Battle of the Netherlands">invaded the Netherlands</a> on 10 May 1940. The <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam_Blitz" title="Rotterdam Blitz">Rotterdam Blitz</a> forced the main element of the Dutch army to surrender four days later. During the occupation, over 100,000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Dutch Jews</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> were rounded up and transported to Nazi <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a> of whom only a few survived. Dutch workers were conscripted for forced labour in Germany, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_resistance" title="Dutch resistance">civilians who resisted</a> were killed in reprisal for attacks on German soldiers, and the countryside was plundered for food. Although there were thousands of Dutch who risked their lives by hiding Jews from the Germans, over 20,000 Dutch fascists <a href="/wiki/23rd_SS_Volunteer_Panzer_Grenadier_Division_Nederland" title="23rd SS Volunteer Panzer Grenadier Division Nederland">joined the Waffen SS</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> fighting on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> Political <a href="/wiki/Collaboration_with_the_Axis_Powers_during_World_War_II" title="Collaboration with the Axis Powers during World War II">collaborators</a> were members of the <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Movement_in_the_Netherlands" title="National Socialist Movement in the Netherlands">NSB</a>, the only legal political party in the occupied Netherlands. On 8 December 1941, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_government-in-exile" title="Dutch government-in-exile">Dutch government-in-exile</a> in London declared war on Japan,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> but could not prevent <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese occupation of Indonesia">the Japanese occupation of the Dutch East Indies (Indonesia)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> In 1944–45, the <a href="/wiki/First_Canadian_Army" title="First Canadian Army">First Canadian Army</a>, which included Canadian, <a href="/wiki/I_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="I Corps (United Kingdom)">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/1st_Armoured_Division_(Poland)" title="1st Armoured Division (Poland)">Polish</a> troops, was responsible for liberating much of the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> But soon after <a href="/wiki/VE_day" class="mw-redirect" title="VE day">VE day</a>, the Dutch fought a <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">colonial war against the new republic of Indonesia</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Netherlands became a co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> predecessors (1993), introduced the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> currency (2002), and signed the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a> in 2007 (pictured).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1954, the <a href="/wiki/Charter_for_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands">Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> reformed the political structure of the Netherlands, which was a result of international pressure to carry out <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a>. The Dutch colonies of <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Surinam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Curaçao and Dependencies">Curaçao and Dependencies</a> and the European country all became countries within the Kingdom, on a basis of equality. Indonesia had declared its independence in August 1945 (recognised in 1949), and thus was never part of the reformed Kingdom. <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> followed in 1975. After the war the Netherlands left behind also an era of neutrality and gained closer ties with neighboring states. The Netherlands was one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euratom" class="mw-redirect" title="Euratom">Euratom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, which would evolve into the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a> (<a href="/wiki/Common_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Common Market">Common Market</a>) and later the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.</p>
<p>Government-encouraged emigration efforts to reduce <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> prompted some 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch people</a> to leave the country after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> The 1960s and 1970s were a time of great social and cultural change, such as rapid <i><a href="/wiki/Pillarization" class="mw-redirect" title="Pillarization">ontzuiling</a></i> (literally: depillarisation), a term that describes the decay of the old divisions along political and religious lines. Youths, and students in particular, rejected traditional mores and pushed for change in matters such as <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_sexuality" title="Human sexuality">sexuality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disarmament" title="Disarmament">disarmament</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental issues">environmental issues</a>. On 10 October 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> was <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">dissolved</a>. Referendums were held on each island to determine their future status. As a result, the islands of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> (the BES islands) were to obtain closer ties with the Netherlands. This led to the incorporation of these three islands into the country of the Netherlands as <i><a href="/wiki/Special_municipality_(Netherlands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Special municipality (Netherlands)">special municipalities</a></i> upon the dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles. The special municipalities are collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Geography of the Netherlands">Geography of the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg/220px-2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg" width="220" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg/330px-2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg/440px-2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="3440" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A relief map of the Netherlands.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The European area of the Netherlands lies between <a href="/wiki/Latitudes" class="mw-redirect" title="Latitudes">latitudes</a> <a href="/wiki/50th_parallel_north" title="50th parallel north">50°</a> and <a href="/wiki/54th_parallel_north" title="54th parallel north">54° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/3rd_meridian_east" title="3rd meridian east">3°</a> and <a href="/wiki/8th_meridian_east" title="8th meridian east">8° E</a>.</p>
<p>The Netherlands is geographically a very low and flat country, with about 26% of its area<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> and 21% of its population<sup id="cite_ref-milrek_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-milrek-69">[67]</a></sup> located below sea level, and only about 50% of its land exceeding one metre <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eupedia_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eupedia-15">[13]</a></sup> The country is for the most part flat, with the exception of foothills in the far southeast, up to a height of no more than 321 metres, and some low hill ranges in the central parts. Most of the areas below sea level are man-made, caused by <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> extraction or achieved through <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>. Since the late 16th century, large <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polder</a> areas are preserved through elaborate drainage systems that include <a href="/wiki/Dike_(construction)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dike (construction)">dikes</a>, canals and pumping stations. Nearly 17% of the country's land area is reclaimed from the sea and from lakes.</p>
<p>Much of the country was originally formed by the <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuaries</a> of three large European rivers: the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> (<i>Rijn</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Meuse_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Meuse River">Meuse</a> (<i>Maas</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> (<i>Schelde</i>), as well as their <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a>. The south-western part of the Netherlands is to this day a <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">river delta</a> of these three rivers, the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Meuse-Scheldt_delta" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine-Meuse-Scheldt delta">Rhine-Meuse-Scheldt delta</a>.</p>
<p>The Netherlands is divided into north and south parts by the Rhine, the <a href="/wiki/Waal_(river)" title="Waal (river)">Waal</a>, its main tributary branch, and the Meuse. In the past these rivers functioned as a natural barrier between <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fiefdoms</a> and hence historically created a cultural divide, as is evident in some phonetic traits that are recognisable on either side of what the Dutch call their "Great Rivers" (<i>de Grote Rivieren</i>). Another significant branch of the Rhine, the <a href="/wiki/IJssel" title="IJssel">IJssel</a> river, discharges into <a href="/wiki/IJsselmeer" title="IJsselmeer">Lake IJssel</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/Zuiderzee" title="Zuiderzee">Zuiderzee</a> ('southern sea'). Just like the previous, this river forms a linguistic divide: people to the northeast of this river speak <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Low_Saxon" title="Dutch Low Saxon">Dutch Low Saxon</a> dialects (except for the province of <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a>, which has its own language).<sup id="cite_ref-international2000_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international2000-70">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Floods">Floods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Floods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Flood_control_in_the_Netherlands" title="Flood control in the Netherlands">Flood control in the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floods_in_the_Netherlands" title="Floods in the Netherlands">Floods in the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_flood_of_1953" title="North Sea flood of 1953">North Sea flood of 1953</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Storm_tides_of_the_North_Sea" title="Storm tides of the North Sea">Storm tides of the North Sea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christmas_flood_1717.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Christmas_flood_1717.jpg/220px-Christmas_flood_1717.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Christmas_flood_1717.jpg/330px-Christmas_flood_1717.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Christmas_flood_1717.jpg/440px-Christmas_flood_1717.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3863" data-file-height="2370" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christmas_flood_1717.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Christmas_flood_of_1717" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas flood of 1717">Christmas flood of 1717</a> was the result of a northwesterly storm. In total, approximately 14,000 people drowned.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over the centuries, the Dutch coastline has changed considerably as a result of natural disasters and human intervention. Most notable in terms of land loss was the storm of 1134, which created the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a> in the south-west.</p>
<p>On 14 December 1287, <a href="/wiki/St._Lucia%27s_flood" title="St. Lucia's flood">St. Lucia's flood</a> affected the Netherlands and Germany killing more than 50,000 people in one of the most destructive floods in recorded history.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/St._Elizabeth%27s_flood_(1421)" title="St. Elizabeth's flood (1421)">St. Elizabeth flood</a> of 1421 and the mismanagement in its aftermath destroyed a newly reclaimed <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polder</a>, replacing it with the 72-square-kilometre (28&#160;sq&#160;mi) <i><a href="/wiki/Biesbosch" class="mw-redirect" title="Biesbosch">Biesbosch</a></i> tidal floodplains in the south-centre. The huge <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_flood_of_1953" title="North Sea flood of 1953">North Sea flood of early February 1953</a> caused the collapse of several dikes in the south-west of the Netherlands; more than 1,800 people drowned in the flood. The Dutch government subsequently instituted a large-scale programme, the "<a href="/wiki/Deltawerken" class="mw-redirect" title="Deltawerken">Delta Works</a>", to protect the country against future flooding, which was completed over a period of more than thirty years.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png/220px-The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png" width="220" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png/330px-The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png/440px-The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png 2x" data-file-width="962" data-file-height="1003" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map illustrating areas of the Netherlands below sea level</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The impact of disasters was to an extent increased through human activity. Relatively high-lying <a href="/wiki/Swamp" title="Swamp">swampland</a> was drained to be used as farmland. The drainage caused the fertile <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> to contract and ground levels to drop, upon which groundwater levels were lowered to compensate for the drop in ground level, causing the underlying peat to contract further. Additionally, until the 19th century peat was mined, dried, and used for fuel, further exacerbating the problem. Centuries of extensive and poorly controlled <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> extraction lowered an already low land surface by several metres. Even in flooded areas, peat extraction continued through turf dredging.</p>
<p>Because of the flooding, farming was difficult, which encouraged foreign trade, the result of which was that the Dutch were involved in world affairs since the early 14th/15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>To guard against floods, a series of defences against the water were contrived. In the first millennium <a href="/wiki/AD" class="mw-redirect" title="AD">AD</a>, villages and farmhouses were built on man-made hills called <i>terps</i>. Later, these terps were connected by dikes. In the 12th century, local government agencies called <i>"<a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">waterschappen</a>"</i> ("water boards") or <i>"<a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">hoogheemraadschappen</a>"</i> ("high home councils") started to appear, whose job it was to maintain the water level and to protect a region from floods; these agencies continue to exist. As the ground level dropped, the dikes by necessity grew and merged into an integrated system. By the 13th century <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmills</a> had come into use to pump water out of areas below sea level. The windmills were later used to drain lakes, creating the famous <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polders</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands,_Zoetermeer,_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_(1).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG/220px-Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG/330px-Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG/440px-Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1716" data-file-height="1140" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands,_Zoetermeer,_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A polder at 5.53 metres below sea level.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1932 the <i><a href="/wiki/Afsluitdijk" title="Afsluitdijk">Afsluitdijk</a></i> ("Closure Dike") was completed, blocking the former <i><a href="/wiki/Zuiderzee" title="Zuiderzee">Zuiderzee</a></i> (Southern Sea) from the North Sea and thus creating the <a href="/wiki/IJsselmeer" title="IJsselmeer">IJsselmeer</a> (<a href="/wiki/IJssel" title="IJssel">IJssel</a> Lake). It became part of the larger <a href="/wiki/Zuiderzee_Works" title="Zuiderzee Works">Zuiderzee Works</a> in which four polders totalling 2,500 square kilometres (965&#160;sq&#160;mi) were reclaimed from the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands is one of the countries that may suffer most from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. Not only is the rising sea a problem, but erratic weather patterns may cause the rivers to overflow.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Delta_works">Delta works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Delta works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Delta_Works" title="Delta Works">Delta Works</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deltawerken_na.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Deltawerken_na.png/220px-Deltawerken_na.png" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Deltawerken_na.png/330px-Deltawerken_na.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Deltawerken_na.png/440px-Deltawerken_na.png 2x" data-file-width="1622" data-file-height="1532" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deltawerken_na.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Delta_Works" title="Delta Works">Delta Works</a> are located in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Flood_of_1953" class="mw-redirect" title="North Sea Flood of 1953">1953 disaster</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Works" title="Delta Works">Delta Works</a> were constructed, a comprehensive set of civil works throughout the Dutch coast. The project started in 1958 and was largely completed in 1997 with the completion of the <a href="/wiki/Maeslantkering" title="Maeslantkering">Maeslantkering</a>. New projects have been periodically started since to renovate and renew the Delta Works. A main goal of the Delta project was to reduce the risk of flooding in South Holland and Zeeland to once per 10,000 years (compared to 1 per 4000 years for the rest of the country). This was achieved by raising 3,000 kilometres (1,864&#160;mi) of outer sea-dykes and 10,000 kilometres (6,214&#160;mi) of inner, canal, and river dikes, and by closing off the sea <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuaries</a> of the Zeeland province. New risk assessments occasionally show problems requiring additional Delta project dyke reinforcements. The Delta project is considered by the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">American Society of Civil Engineers</a> as one of the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers#World_wonders" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">seven wonders of the modern world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is anticipated that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> in the 21st century will result in a rise in <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. The Netherlands is actively preparing for a sea level rise (see <a href="/wiki/Flood_control_in_the_Netherlands" title="Flood control in the Netherlands">Flood control in the Netherlands</a>). A politically neutral Delta Commission has formulated an action plan to cope with a sea level rise of 1.10 metres (3.6&#160;ft) and a simultaneous land height decline of 10 centimetres (3.9&#160;in). The plan encompasses the reinforcement of the existing coastal defenses like <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">dikes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">dunes</a> with 1.30 metres (4.3&#160;ft) of additional flood protection. Climate change will not only threaten the Netherlands from the sea side, but could also alter rain fall patterns and river run-off. To protect the country from river flooding, another program is already being executed. The <a href="/wiki/Room_for_the_River_(Netherlands)" title="Room for the River (Netherlands)">Room for the River plan</a> grants more flow space to rivers, protects the major populated areas and allows for periodic flooding of indefensible lands. The few residents who lived in these so-called "overflow areas" have been moved to higher ground, with some of that ground having been raised above anticipated flood levels.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT021313_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT021313-79">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The predominant wind direction in the Netherlands is southwest, which causes a moderate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a>, with warm summers and cool winters, and typically high humidity. This is especially true close to the Dutch coastline, where the difference in temperature between summer and winter, as well as between day and night is noticeably smaller than it is in the southeast of the country.</p>
<p>The following tables are based on mean measurements by the <a href="/wiki/KNMI_(institute)" class="mw-redirect" title="KNMI (institute)">KNMI</a> weather station in <a href="/wiki/De_Bilt" title="De Bilt">De Bilt</a> between 1981 and 2010:</p>

<tr>
<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: Knmi.nl<sup id="cite_ref-knmi_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knmi-80">[78]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Ice days (maximum temperature below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F)) usually occur from December until February, with the occasional rare ice day prior to or after that period. Freezing days (minimum temperature below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F)) occur much more often, usually ranging from mid-November to late March, but not rarely measured as early as mid-October and as late as mid-May. If one chooses the height of measurement to be 10&#160;cm (4&#160;in) above ground instead of 150&#160;cm (59&#160;in), one may even find such temperatures in the middle of the summer. On average, snow can occur from November to April, but sometimes occurs in May or October too.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg/220px-Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg/330px-Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg/440px-Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3539" data-file-height="2654" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Warm days (maximum temperature above 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F)) in De Bilt are usually found in April to October, but in some parts of the country these warm days can also occur in March, or even sometimes in November or February (usually not in De Bilt, however). Summer days (maximum temperature above 25&#160;°C (77&#160;°F)) are usually measured in De Bilt from May until September, tropical days (maximum temperature above 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F)) are rare and usually occur only in June to August.</p>
<p>Precipitation throughout the year is distributed relatively equally each month. Summer and autumn months tend to gather a little more precipitation than the other months, mainly because of the intensity of the rainfall rather than the frequency of rain days (this is especially the case in summer, when lightning is also much more frequent).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg/220px-Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg/330px-Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg/440px-Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Netherlands_Grote_Peel_lake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/De_Groote_Peel_National_Park" title="De Groote Peel National Park">De Groote Peel National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The number of sunshine hours is affected by the fact that because of the geographical latitude, the length of the days varies between barely eight hours in December and nearly 17 hours in June.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature">Nature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Nature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of national parks of the Netherlands">List of national parks of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_extinct_animals_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of extinct animals of the Netherlands">List of extinct animals of the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>The Netherlands has 20 national parks and hundreds of other nature reserves, that include <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heathland" class="mw-redirect" title="Heathland">heathland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodland" title="Woodland">woods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">dunes</a> and other habitats. Most of these are owned by <a href="/wiki/Staatsbosbeheer" title="Staatsbosbeheer">Staatsbosbeheer</a>, the national department for <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habitat_conservation" title="Habitat conservation">nature conservation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vereniging_Natuurmonumenten" title="Vereniging Natuurmonumenten">Natuurmonumenten</a> (literally 'Natures monuments'), a private organisation that buys, protects and manages nature reserves. The Dutch part of the <a href="/wiki/Wadden_Sea" title="Wadden Sea">Wadden Sea</a> in the north, with its <a href="/wiki/Tidal_flat" class="mw-redirect" title="Tidal flat">tidal flats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a>, is rich in <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biological diversity</a>, and was declared a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Nature Site</a> in 2009.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg/220px-Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg/330px-Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg/440px-Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2856" data-file-height="1707" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Harbor_seal" title="Harbor seal">Common seals</a> on <a href="/wiki/Terschelling" title="Terschelling">Terschelling</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Wadden_Sea" title="Wadden Sea">Wadden Sea</a> island</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Oosterschelde" class="mw-redirect" title="Oosterschelde">Oosterschelde</a>, formerly the northeast <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> of the river <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> was designated a national park in 2002, thereby making it the largest national park in the Netherlands at an area of 370 square kilometres (140&#160;sq&#160;mi). It consists primarily of the salt waters of the Oosterschelde, but also includes mud flats, meadows, and shoals. Because of the large variety of sea life, including unique regional species, the park is popular with <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">Scuba divers</a>. Other activities include sailing, fishing, cycling, and bird watching.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, the Netherlands is shared between the Atlantic European and Central European provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a>, the territory of the Netherlands belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of Atlantic mixed forests. In 1871, the last old original natural woods were cut down, and most woods today are planted monocultures of trees like <a href="/wiki/Scots_pine" title="Scots pine">Scots pine</a> and trees that are not native to the Netherlands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These woods were planted on <a href="/wiki/Heath_(habitat)#Anthropogenic_heaths" class="mw-redirect" title="Heath (habitat)">anthropogenic heaths</a> and sand-drifts (overgrazed heaths) (<a href="/wiki/Veluwe" title="Veluwe">Veluwe</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean_islands">Caribbean islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Caribbean islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a> are three islands designated as special municipalities of the Netherlands. The islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>. The islands have maritime borders with <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>), the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>), <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<a href="/wiki/US_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="US Virgin Islands">US Virgin Islands</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup><br />
Within this island group,</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bonaire_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Bonaire_1.jpg/220px-Bonaire_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Bonaire_1.jpg/330px-Bonaire_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Bonaire_1.jpg/440px-Bonaire_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1664" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bonaire_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the coast of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b>Bonaire</b> is part of the <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC islands</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Antilles" title="Leeward Antilles">Leeward Antilles</a> island chain off the <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuelan</a> coast. The Leeward Antilles have a mixed volcanic and coral origin.</li>
<li><b>Saba</b> and <b>Sint Eustatius</b> are part of the <a href="/wiki/SSS_islands" title="SSS islands">SSS islands</a>. They are located east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a>. Although in the English language they are considered part of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, French, Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> and the English spoken locally consider them part of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>. The Windward Islands are all of volcanic origin and hilly, leaving little ground suitable for <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Scenery" title="Mount Scenery">Mount Scenery</a>, 887 metres (2,910&#160;ft), on <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>. This is the highest point in the country, and is also the highest point of the entire <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The islands of the Caribbean Netherlands enjoy a <a href="/wiki/Tropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical">tropical</a> <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> with warm weather all year round. The Leeward Antilles are warmer and drier than the Windward islands. In summer, the Windward Islands can be subject to <a href="/wiki/Hurricanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricanes">hurricanes</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg/220px-Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg/330px-Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg/440px-Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Den_Haag_Binnenhof.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Binnenhof" title="Binnenhof">Binnenhof</a>, where the lower and upper houses of the States General meet</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands has been a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> since 1815 and a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a> since 1848. The Netherlands is described as a <a href="/wiki/Consociational_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Consociational state">consociational state</a>. Dutch politics and governance are characterised by an effort to achieve broad consensus on important issues, within both the political community and society as a whole. In 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> ranked the Netherlands as the 10th <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">most democratic country in the world</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch monarchy">monarch</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, at present <a href="/wiki/King_Willem-Alexander" class="mw-redirect" title="King Willem-Alexander">King Willem-Alexander</a>. Constitutionally, the position is equipped with limited powers. By law, the king (the title queen has no constitutional significance) has the right to be periodically briefed and consulted on government affairs. Depending on the personalities and relationships of the king and the ministers, the king might have <i>influence</i> beyond the <i>power</i> granted by the constitution.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willem-Alexander_(Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm,_2010)_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg/170px-Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg/255px-Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg/340px-Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="789" data-file-height="1152" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willem-Alexander_(Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm,_2010)_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Willem-Alexander_of_the_Netherlands" title="Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands">Willem-Alexander</a>, King of the Netherlands since 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a> is formed by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of the Netherlands">council of Ministers</a>, the deliberative council of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_Netherlands" title="Cabinet of the Netherlands">Dutch cabinet</a>. The cabinet usually consists of 13 to 16 ministers and a varying number of <a href="/wiki/State_Secretary_(Netherlands)" class="mw-redirect" title="State Secretary (Netherlands)">state secretaries</a>. One to three ministers are <a href="/wiki/Minister_without_portfolio" title="Minister without portfolio">ministers without portfolio</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Netherlands" title="Prime Minister of the Netherlands">Prime Minister of the Netherlands</a>, who often is the leader of the largest party of the coalition. The Prime Minister is a <i><a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares" title="Primus inter pares">primus inter pares</a></i>, with no explicit powers beyond those of the other ministers. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rutte" title="Mark Rutte">Mark Rutte</a> has been Prime Minister since October 2010; the Prime Minister had been the leader of the largest party continuously since 1973.</p>
<p>The cabinet is <a href="/wiki/Ministerial_responsibility" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministerial responsibility">responsible</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> parliament, the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General</a>, which also has <a href="/wiki/Legislative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative">legislative powers</a>. The 150 members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of the Netherlands">House of Representatives</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lower_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower House">Lower House</a>, are elected in <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">direct elections</a> on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>. These are held every four years, or sooner in case the cabinet falls (for example: when one of the chambers carries a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">motion of no confidence</a>, the cabinet offers its resignation to the monarch). The <a href="/wiki/States-Provincial" title="States-Provincial">States-Provincial</a> are directly elected every four years as well. The members of the provincial assemblies elect the 75 members of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of the Netherlands">Senate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a>, which has the power to reject laws, but not propose or amend them.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Both trade unions and <a href="/wiki/Employers_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Employers organisation">employers organisations</a> are consulted beforehand in policymaking in the financial, economic and social areas. They meet regularly with government in the <a href="/wiki/Social-Economic_Council" title="Social-Economic Council">Social-Economic Council</a>. This body advises government and its advice cannot be put aside easily.</p>
<p>The Netherlands has a long tradition of <a href="/wiki/Toleration" title="Toleration">social tolerance</a>. In the 18th century, while the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a> was the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in the Netherlands">Catholicism</a>, other forms of Protestantism, such as Baptists and Lutherans, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Judaism</a> were tolerated but discriminated against.</p>
<p>In the late 19th century this Dutch tradition of religious tolerance transformed into a system of <a href="/wiki/Pillarisation" title="Pillarisation">pillarisation</a>, in which religious groups coexisted separately and only interacted at the level of government. This tradition of tolerance influences Dutch <a href="/wiki/Criminal_justice_system_of_the_Netherlands" title="Criminal justice system of the Netherlands">criminal justice</a> policies on <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">recreational drugs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Netherlands" title="Prostitution in the Netherlands">prostitution</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_Netherlands" title="LGBT rights in the Netherlands">LGBT rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_Netherlands" title="Abortion in the Netherlands">abortion</a>, which are among the most liberal in the world.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_parties">Political parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Political parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Political_parties_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Political parties of the Netherlands">Political parties of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Netherlands" title="Politics of the Netherlands">Politics of the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Rutte-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mark_Rutte-4.jpg/170px-Mark_Rutte-4.jpg" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mark_Rutte-4.jpg/255px-Mark_Rutte-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mark_Rutte-4.jpg/340px-Mark_Rutte-4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3394" data-file-height="4724" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Rutte-4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mark_Rutte" title="Mark Rutte">Mark Rutte</a>, Prime Minister of the Netherlands since October 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because of the <a href="/wiki/Political_parties_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Political parties of the Netherlands">multi-party system</a>, no single party has held a majority in parliament since the 19th century, and <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition cabinets</a> had to be formed. Since <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> became universal in 1919, the Dutch political system has been dominated by three families of political parties: the strongest of which were the <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian democrats</a>, currently represented by the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Appeal" title="Christian Democratic Appeal">Christian Democratic Appeal</a> (CDA); second were the <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democrats</a>, represented by the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Labour Party">Labour Party</a> (PvdA); and third were the <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_in_the_Netherlands" title="Liberalism in the Netherlands">liberals</a>, of which the right wing <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_for_Freedom_and_Democracy" title="People's Party for Freedom and Democracy">People's Party for Freedom and Democracy</a> (VVD) is the main representative.</p>
<p>These parties co-operated in coalition cabinets in which the Christian democrats had always been a partner: so either a <a href="/wiki/Centre-left" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-left">centre-left</a> coalition of the Christian democrats and social democrats was ruling or a <a href="/wiki/Centre-right" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-right">centre-right</a> coalition of Christian democrats and liberals. In the 1970s, the <a href="/wiki/Party_system" title="Party system">party system</a> became more volatile: the Christian democratic parties lost seats, while new parties became successful, such as the <a href="/wiki/Radicalism_(historical)" title="Radicalism (historical)">radical</a> democrat and <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> liberal <a href="/wiki/D%2766" class="mw-redirect" title="D'66">D66</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_1994" title="Dutch general election, 1994">1994 election</a>, the CDA lost its dominant position. A "<a href="/wiki/Purple_(government)" title="Purple (government)">purple</a>" cabinet was formed by VVD, D66, and PvdA. In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2002" title="Dutch general election, 2002">2002 elections</a>, this cabinet lost its majority, because of an increased support for the CDA and the rise of the right <a href="/wiki/Lijst_Pim_Fortuyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Lijst Pim Fortuyn">LPF</a>, a new political party, around <a href="/wiki/Pim_Fortuyn" title="Pim Fortuyn">Pim Fortuyn</a>, who was assassinated a week before the elections. A short-lived <a href="/wiki/First_Balkenende_cabinet" title="First Balkenende cabinet">cabinet</a> was formed by CDA, VVD, and LPF, which was led by the CDA leader <a href="/wiki/Jan_Peter_Balkenende" title="Jan Peter Balkenende">Jan Peter Balkenende</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2003" title="Dutch general election, 2003">2003 elections</a>, in which the LPF lost most of its seats, a <a href="/wiki/Balkenende_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkenende II">cabinet</a> was formed by CDA, VVD, and D66. The cabinet initiated an ambitious programme of reforming the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_Netherlands" title="Healthcare in the Netherlands">healthcare system</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_policy" title="Immigration policy">immigration policy</a>.</p>
<p>In June 2006, the cabinet fell after D66 voted in favour of a motion of no confidence against the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Security_and_Justice_(Netherlands)" title="Ministry of Security and Justice (Netherlands)">Minister of Immigration and Integration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_Verdonk" title="Rita Verdonk">Rita Verdonk</a>, who had instigated an investigation of the asylum procedure of <a href="/wiki/Ayaan_Hirsi_Ali" title="Ayaan Hirsi Ali">Ayaan Hirsi Ali</a>, a VVD <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">MP</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Balkenende_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkenende III">caretaker cabinet</a> was formed by CDA and VVD, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2006" title="Dutch general election, 2006">general elections</a> were held on 22 November 2006. In these elections, the CDA remained the largest party and the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Socialist Party (Netherlands)">Socialist Party</a> made the largest gains. The <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Dutch_cabinet_formation" title="2006–07 Dutch cabinet formation">formation of a new cabinet</a> took three months, resulting in a <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_cabinet_Balkenende-4" class="mw-redirect" title="Netherlands cabinet Balkenende-4">coalition</a> of CDA, PvdA, and <a href="/wiki/ChristianUnion" class="mw-redirect" title="ChristianUnion">ChristianUnion</a>.</p>
<p>On 20 February 2010, the cabinet fell when the PvdA refused to prolong the involvement of the Dutch Army in <a href="/wiki/Uruzgan" class="mw-redirect" title="Uruzgan">Uruzgan</a>, Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Snap_election" title="Snap election">Snap elections</a> were held on <a href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2010" title="Dutch general election, 2010">9 June 2010</a>, with devastating results for the previously largest party, the CDA, which lost about half of its seats, resulting in 21 seats. The VVD became the largest party with 31 seats, closely followed by the PvdA with 30 seats. The big winner of the 2010 elections was <a href="/wiki/Geert_Wilders" title="Geert Wilders">Geert Wilders</a>, whose right wing <a href="/wiki/Party_for_Freedom" title="Party for Freedom">PVV</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> the ideological successor to the <a href="/wiki/Pim_Fortuyn_List" title="Pim Fortuyn List">LPF</a>, more than doubled its number of seats.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2010_Dutch_cabinet_formation" title="2010 Dutch cabinet formation">Negotiation talks for a new government</a> resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority government</a>, led by VVD (a first) in coalition with CDA, which was sworn in on 14 October 2010. This unprecedented minority government was supported by PVV, but proved ultimately to be unstable,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> when on 21 April 2012, Wilders, leader of PVV, unexpectedly 'torpedoed seven weeks of austerity talks' on new austerity measures, paving the way for early elections.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>VVD and PvdA were the big winners of the elections. Since 5 November 2012 they have formed the <a href="/wiki/Second_Rutte_cabinet" title="Second Rutte cabinet">second Rutte cabinet</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the Netherlands">Government of the Netherlands</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Provinces of the Netherlands">Provinces of the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of the Netherlands">Municipalities of the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">Water board (Netherlands)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_body_(Netherlands)" title="Public body (Netherlands)">Public body (Netherlands)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg/330px-Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg.png" width="330" height="391" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg/495px-Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg/660px-Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="743" data-file-height="881" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Provinces of the Netherlands">Provinces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Special_municipality_(Netherlands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Special municipality (Netherlands)">special municipalities</a> of the Netherlands.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands is divided into twelve provinces, each under a Commissioner of the King (<i>Commissaris van de Koning</i>), except for <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg province</a> where the position is named Governor (<i>Gouverneur</i>). All provinces are divided into <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of the Netherlands">municipalities</a> (<i>gemeenten</i>), of which there are 388 (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-MUNICPS_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUNICPS-90">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The country is also subdivided into 24 water districts, governed by a <a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">water board</a> (<i>waterschap</i> or <i>hoogheemraadschap</i>), each having authority in matters concerning water management.<sup id="cite_ref-WATER_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WATER-91">[89]</a></sup> The creation of water boards actually pre-dates that of the nation itself, the first appearing in 1196. The Dutch water boards are among the oldest democratic entities in the world still in existence. Direct elections of the water boards take place every 4 years.</p>
<p>The administrative structure on the 3 BES islands, collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>, is different. These islands have the status of <i>openbare lichamen (<a href="/wiki/Public_body_(Netherlands)" title="Public body (Netherlands)">public bodies</a>)</i> rather than municipalities and as administrative units are generally referred to as <i>special municipalities</i>. They are not part of a province.<sup id="cite_ref-WOLBES_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WOLBES-92">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands has several Belgian <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclaves</a> <sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> and within those even several enclaves which are still part of the province of <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a>. Because the Netherlands and <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> are both in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, citizens of respective countries can easily travel through these enclaves.</p>
