<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:International_Court_of_Justice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/International_Court_of_Justice.jpg/220px-International_Court_of_Justice.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/International_Court_of_Justice.jpg/330px-International_Court_of_Justice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/International_Court_of_Justice.jpg/440px-International_Court_of_Justice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="597" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:International_Court_of_Justice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Peace_Palace" title="Peace Palace">Peace Palace</a> (<i>Vredespaleis</i>), <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Netherlands" title="Foreign relations of the Netherlands">Foreign relations of the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>The history of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Netherlands" title="Foreign relations of the Netherlands">Dutch foreign policy</a> has been characterised by its <a href="/wiki/Neutral_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutral state">neutrality</a>. Since World War II, the Netherlands has become a member of a large number of international organisations, most prominently the UN, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the EU. The Dutch economy is very open and relies strongly on <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> of the Netherlands is based on four basic commitments: to <a href="/wiki/Atlanticism" title="Atlanticism">Atlantic co-operation</a>, to <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>, to <a href="/wiki/International_development" title="International development">international development</a> and to <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>. One of the more controversial international issues surrounding the Netherlands is its <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">liberal policy towards soft drugs</a>.</p>
<p>During and after the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>, the Dutch people built up a commercial and colonial empire. The most important colonies were present-day <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. Indonesia became independent after the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">Indonesian National Revolution</a> in the 1940s following a war of independence, international pressure and several <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolutions" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council Resolutions">UN Security Council Resolutions</a>. Suriname became independent in 1975. The historical ties inherited from its colonial past still influence the foreign relations of the Netherlands. In addition, many people from these countries are living permanently in the Netherlands.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Armed forces of the Netherlands">Armed forces of the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>The Netherlands has one of the oldest standing armies in Europe; it was first established as such by <a href="/wiki/Maurice_of_Nassau" class="mw-redirect" title="Maurice of Nassau">Maurice of Nassau</a>. The Dutch army was used throughout the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a>. After the defeat of Napoleon, the Dutch army was transformed into a <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> army. The army was unsuccessfully deployed during the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a> in 1830. After 1830, it was deployed mainly in the Dutch colonies, as the Netherlands remained neutral in European wars (including the First World War), until the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Netherlands" title="Battle of the Netherlands">Netherlands was invaded in World War II</a> and quickly defeated by the Wehrmacht in May 1940.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HNLMS_Holland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/HNLMS_Holland.jpg/220px-HNLMS_Holland.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/HNLMS_Holland.jpg/330px-HNLMS_Holland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/HNLMS_Holland.jpg/440px-HNLMS_Holland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HNLMS_Holland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Zr. Ms. Holland</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Dutch Navy">Royal Dutch Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Offshore_patrol_vessel" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore patrol vessel">offshore patrol vessel</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands abandoned its neutrality in 1948 when it signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a>, and became a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in 1949. The Dutch military was therefore part of the NATO strength in <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> Europe, deploying its army to several bases in Germany. More than 3,000 Dutch soldiers were assigned to the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="2nd Infantry Division (United States)">2nd Infantry Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>. In 1996 conscription was suspended, and the Dutch army was once again transformed into a professional army. Since the 1990s the Dutch army has been involved in the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, it held a province in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> after the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>, and it was engaged in <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">Afghanistan</a>.</p>
<p>The military is composed of four branches, all of which carry the prefix <i>Koninklijke</i> (Royal):</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Koninklijke Landmacht</i> (KL), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Army" title="Royal Netherlands Army">Royal Netherlands Army</a></li>
<li><i>Koninklijke Marine</i> (KM), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">Royal Netherlands Navy</a>, including the Naval Air Service and Marine Corps</li>
<li><i>Koninklijke Luchtmacht</i> (KLu), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Air_Force" title="Royal Netherlands Air Force">Royal Netherlands Air Force</a></li>
<li><i>Koninklijke Marechaussee</i> (KMar), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marechaussee" title="Royal Marechaussee">Royal Marechaussee</a> (Military Police), tasks include military police and border control</li>
</ul>
<p>General <a href="/wiki/Tom_Middendorp" title="Tom Middendorp">Tom Middendorp</a> is the current Commander of the Netherlands armed forces. The <a href="/wiki/Koninklijke_Marine#Submarine_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Koninklijke Marine">submarine service</a> are open to women as of 1 January 2017. <a href="/wiki/Korps_Commandotroepen" title="Korps Commandotroepen">The Korps Commandotroepen</a>, the Special Operations Force of the Netherlands Army, is open to women, but because of the extremely high physical demands for initial training, it is almost impossible for women to become a commando.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> The Dutch Ministry of Defence employs more than 70,000 personnel, including over 20,000 civilians and over 50,000 military personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> In April 2011 the government announced a major reduction in its military because of a cut in government expenditure, including a decrease in the number of tanks, fighter aircraft, naval ships and senior officials.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Economy of the Netherlands">Economy of the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazonehaven.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Amazonehaven.JPG/220px-Amazonehaven.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Amazonehaven.JPG/330px-Amazonehaven.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Amazonehaven.JPG/440px-Amazonehaven.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazonehaven.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">Port of Rotterdam</a> is Europe's largest port.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands has a developed economy and has been playing a special role in the European economy for many centuries. Since the 16th century, shipping, fishing, agriculture, trade, and banking have been leading sectors of the Dutch economy. The Netherlands has <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_freedom" title="List of countries by economic freedom">a high level of economic freedom</a>. The Netherlands is one of the top countries in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Enabling_Trade_Report" title="Global Enabling Trade Report">Global Enabling Trade Report</a> (3rd in 2014).</p>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the key trading partners of the Netherlands were Germany, Belgium, UK, United States, France, Italy, China and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> The Netherlands is one of the world's 10 leading exporting countries. Foodstuffs form the largest industrial sector. Other major industries include chemicals, metallurgy, machinery, electrical goods, trade, services and tourism. Examples of international Dutch companies operating in Netherlands include <a href="/wiki/Randstad_Holding" title="Randstad Holding">Randstad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heineken_International" title="Heineken International">Heineken</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, financial services (<a href="/wiki/ING_Group" title="ING Group">ING</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABN_AMRO" title="ABN AMRO">ABN AMRO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabobank" title="Rabobank">Rabobank</a>), chemicals (<a href="/wiki/DSM_(company)" title="DSM (company)">DSM</a>, <a href="/wiki/AkzoNobel" title="AkzoNobel">AKZO</a>), petroleum refining (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a>), electronical machinery (<a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASML_Holding" title="ASML Holding">ASML</a>), and car navigation (<a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">TomTom</a>).</p>
<p>The Netherlands has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">17th-largest economy in the world</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">ranks 10th in GDP (nominal) per capita</a>. Between 1997 and 2000 annual economic growth (GDP) averaged nearly 4%, well above the European average. Growth slowed considerably from 2001 to 2005 with the global economic slowdown, but accelerated to 4.1% in the third quarter of 2007. In May 2013, inflation was at 2.8% per year.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> In April 2013, unemployment was at 8.2% (or 6.7% following the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">ILO</a> definition) of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour force">labour force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> In January 2017, this was reduced to 5.3%.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Quarter_(time)" class="mw-redirect" title="Quarter (time)">Q3</a> and Q4 2011, the Dutch economy contracted by 0.4% and 0.7%, respectively, because of European Debt Crisis, while in Q4 the Eurozone economy shrunk by 0.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> The Netherlands also has a relatively low <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">GINI coefficient</a> of 0.326. Despite ranking 7th in <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> ranked the Netherlands 1st in child well-being.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a> Netherlands is the 13th most <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> capitalist economy out of 157 surveyed countries.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> is the financial and business capital of the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-ez_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ez-106">[104]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> (AEX), part of <a href="/wiki/Euronext" title="Euronext">Euronext</a>, is the world's oldest stock exchange and is one of Europe's largest bourses. It is situated near <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a> in the city's centre. As a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, the Netherlands replaced (for accounting purposes) its former currency, the "gulden" (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">guilder</a>), on 1 January 1999, along with 15 other adopters of the euro. Actual <a href="/wiki/Euro_coins" title="Euro coins">euro coins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">banknotes</a> followed on 1 January 2002. One euro was equivalent to 2.20371 Dutch guilders. In the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> is used instead of the euro.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/220px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/330px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/440px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="645" data-file-height="690" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Netherlands is part of a monetary union, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> (dark blue), and of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Market_(European_Union)" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal Market (European Union)">EU single market</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Dutch location gives it prime access to markets in the UK and Germany, with the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">port of Rotterdam</a> being the largest port in Europe. Other important parts of the economy are <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a> (Dutch colonialism started with co-operative private enterprises such as the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">VOC</a>), banking and transport. The Netherlands successfully addressed the issue of public finances and stagnating job growth long before its European partners. Amsterdam is the 5th-busiest tourist destination in Europe with more than 4.2&#160;million international visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-42milvisitors_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42milvisitors-107">[105]</a></sup> Since the enlargement of the EU large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Migrant_worker" title="Migrant worker">migrant workers</a> have arrived in the Netherlands from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">eastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of economic importance is <a href="/wiki/BrabantStad" title="BrabantStad">BrabantStad</a>, a partnership between the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Breda" title="Breda">Breda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helmond" title="Helmond">Helmond</a>, <a href="/wiki/%27s-Hertogenbosch" title="'s-Hertogenbosch">'s-Hertogenbosch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tilburg" title="Tilburg">Tilburg</a> and the province of North Brabant. BrabantStad is the fastest growing economic region in the Netherlands, with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brainport_(Netherlands)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brainport (Netherlands) (page does not exist)">Brainport</a> as one of the three national top regions. The region lies within the <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a>-<a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>-<a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> Triangle (ELAT).<sup id="cite_ref-ref608454752_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref608454752-109">[107]</a></sup> The partnership aims to form an urban network and to make North Brabant explicitly known as a leading knowledge region within Europe. With a total of 1.5&#160;million people and 20% of the industrial production in the Netherlands is BrabantStad one of the major economical important, metropolitan regions of the Netherlands. Of all the money that goes to research and development in the Netherlands, one third is spent in <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a>. A quarter of the jobs in the region are in technology and ICT.<sup id="cite_ref-ref-213874478_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref-213874478-110">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of all European patent applications in the field of physics and electronics about eight per cent is from North Brabant.<sup id="cite_ref-ref-601915138_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref-601915138-111">[109]</a></sup> In the extended region, BrabantStad is part of the <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a>-<a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>-<a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> Triangle (ELAT). This economic cooperation agreement between three cities in three countries has created one of the most innovative regions in the European Union (measured in terms of money invested in <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_economy" title="Knowledge economy">knowledge economy</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ref1983490620_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref1983490620-112">[110]</a></sup> The economic success of this region is important for the international competitiveness of the Netherlands; Together <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">airport</a>), <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">seaport</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a> form the foundation of the Dutch economy.<sup id="cite_ref-ref1367203750_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref1367203750-113">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands continues to be one of the leading European nations for attracting foreign direct investment and is one of the five largest investors in the United States. The economy experienced a slowdown in 2005, but in 2006 recovered to the fastest pace in six years on the back of increased exports and strong investment. The pace of job growth reached 10-year highs in 2007. The Netherlands is the fifth-most competitive economy in the world, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wefcomp_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wefcomp-114">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_gas">Natural gas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Natural gas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Natural_gas_NL.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Natural_gas_NL.png/220px-Natural_gas_NL.png" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Natural_gas_NL.png/330px-Natural_gas_NL.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Natural_gas_NL.png/440px-Natural_gas_NL.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1032" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Natural_gas_NL.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Natural gas concessions in the Netherlands. Today the Netherlands accounts for more than 25% of all Natural Gas reserves in the EU</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beginning in the 1950s, the Netherlands discovered huge natural gas resources. The sale of natural gas generated enormous revenues for the Netherlands for decades to come, adding hundreds of billions of euros to the government's budget.<sup id="cite_ref-vorige.nrc.nl_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vorige.nrc.nl-115">[113]</a></sup> However, the unforeseen consequences of the country's huge energy wealth impacted the competitiveness of other sectors of the economy, leading to the theory of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_disease" title="Dutch disease">Dutch disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vorige.nrc.nl_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vorige.nrc.nl-115">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Apart from coal and gas, the country has no mining resources. The last coal mine was closed in 1974. The <a href="/wiki/Groningen_gas_field" title="Groningen gas field">Groningen gas field</a>, one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_field" title="Natural gas field">natural gas fields</a> in the world, is situated near <a href="/wiki/Slochteren" title="Slochteren">Slochteren</a>. Exploitation of this field has resulted in €159&#160;billion in revenue since the mid-1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-geo_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geo-116">[114]</a></sup> The field is operated by government-owned Gasunie and output is jointly exploited by the government, Royal Dutch Shell, and Exxon Mobil through NAM (Nederlandse Aardolie Maatschappij). "Gas extraction has resulted in increasingly strong earth tremors, some measuring as much as 3.6 on the Richter magnitude scale. The cost of damage repairs, structural improvements to buildings, and compensation for home value decreases has been estimated at 6.5 billion euros. Around 35,000 homes are said to be affected."<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> The Netherlands have an estimated 25% of natural gas reserves in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bollenvelden_bij_De_Zilk.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dutch flower fields near De Zilk</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Dutch agricultural sector is highly mechanised, and has a strong focus on international exports. It employs about 4% of the Dutch labour force but produces large surpluses for the food-processing industry and accounts for 21 percent of the Dutch total export value.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> The Dutch rank second worldwide in value of agricultural exports, behind only the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> with exports earning €80.7&#160;billion in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-government.nl_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-government.nl-121">[119]</a></sup> up from €75.4&#160;billion in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-hollandtrade.com_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollandtrade.com-17">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands has, at some time in recent history, supplied one quarter of all of the world's exported tomatoes, and trade of one-third of the world's exports of <a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">chilis</a>, tomatoes and cucumbers goes through the country. The Netherlands also exports one-fifteenth of the world's apples.<sup id="cite_ref-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aside from that, a significant portion of Dutch agricultural exports consists of fresh-cut plants, flowers, and flower bulbs, with the Netherlands exporting two-thirds of the world's total.<sup id="cite_ref-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NederlandA15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/NederlandA15.jpg/220px-NederlandA15.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/NederlandA15.jpg/330px-NederlandA15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/NederlandA15.jpg/440px-NederlandA15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NederlandA15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Highway A15 / A16 <a href="/wiki/Overpass" title="Overpass">flyover</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Netherlands" title="Transport in the Netherlands">Transport in the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>Mobility on Dutch roads has grown continuously since the 1950s and now exceeds 200 billion km travelled per year,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> three quarters of which are done by car.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-124">[122]</a></sup> Around half of all trips in the Netherlands are made by car, 25% by bicycle, 20% walking, and 5% by public transport.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-124">[122]</a></sup> With a total <a href="/wiki/Roads_in_the_Netherlands" title="Roads in the Netherlands">road network</a> of 139,295&#160;km, which includes 2,758&#160;km of expressways,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> the Netherlands has one of the densest road networks in the world—much denser than <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, but still not as dense as <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>About 13% of all distance is travelled by public transport, the majority of which by train.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-124">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_rail_transport_network_size" title="List of countries by rail transport network size">Like in many other European countries</a>, the Dutch rail network of 3,013 route&#160;km is also rather dense.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> The network is mostly focused on passenger rail services and connects virtually all major towns and cities. Trains are frequent, with one or two trains per hour on lesser lines, two to four trains per hour on average, and up to eight trains an hour on the busiest lines.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fietsstraat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Fietsstraat.jpg/220px-Fietsstraat.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Fietsstraat.jpg/330px-Fietsstraat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Fietsstraat.jpg/440px-Fietsstraat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="429" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fietsstraat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_the_Netherlands#Fietsstraat_.28bike_street.29" title="Cycling in the Netherlands"><i>fietsstraat</i></a> (bike street) where cyclists have priority and cars are "guests" and must yield.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_the_Netherlands" title="Cycling in the Netherlands">Cycling</a> is a ubiquitous mode of transport in the Netherlands. Almost as many kilometres are covered by bicycle as by train.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-124">[122]</a></sup> The Dutch are estimated to have at least 18 million bicycles,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> which makes more than one per capita, and twice as many as the c. 9 million motor vehicles on the road.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/European_Cyclists%27_Federation" title="European Cyclists' Federation">European Cyclists' Federation</a> ranked both the Netherlands and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> as the most bike-friendly countries in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> but more of the Dutch (36%) than of the Danes (23%) list the bike as their most frequent mode of transport on a typical day.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[nb 3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cycling_infrastructure" title="Cycling infrastructure">Cycling infrastructure</a> is comprehensive. Busy roads have received some 35,000&#160;km of <a href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities" class="mw-redirect" title="Segregated cycle facilities">dedicated cycle tracks</a>, physically segregated from motorised traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup> Busy junctions are often equipped with bicycle-specific traffic lights. There are large bicycle parking facilities, particularly in city centres and at train stations.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> has the largest port in Europe, with the rivers Meuse and Rhine providing excellent access to the <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a> upstream reaching to <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>, Switzerland, and into France. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Rotterdam was the world's eighth largest <a href="/wiki/Container_port" class="mw-redirect" title="Container port">container port</a> handling 440.5 million metric tonnes of cargo annually.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup> The port's main activities are <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemical</a> industries and general cargo handling and <a href="/wiki/Transshipment" title="Transshipment">transshipment</a>. The harbour functions as an important transit point for <a href="/wiki/Bulk_material_handling" title="Bulk material handling">bulk materials</a> and between the European continent and overseas. From Rotterdam goods are transported by ship, river barge, train or road. In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Betuweroute" title="Betuweroute">Betuweroute</a>, a new fast freight railway from Rotterdam to Germany, was completed.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Schiphol airport</a>, just southwest of Amsterdam, is the main <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in the Netherlands, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">third busiest airport in Europe</a> in terms of passengers. In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a> airports handled 70 million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-NOS_Schiphol64_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOS_Schiphol64-138">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>As part of its commitment to environmental sustainability, the Dutch government initiated a plan to establish over 200 recharging stations for electric vehicles across the country by 2015. The rollout will be undertaken by Switzerland-based power and automation company ABB and Dutch startup Fastned, and will aim to provide at least one station within a 50-kilometre radius (30 miles) from every home in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Netherlands" title="Demographics of the Netherlands">Demographics of the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png/220px-Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png/330px-Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2c/Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png 2x" data-file-width="416" data-file-height="313" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Population of the Netherlands from 1900 to 2000.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Netherlands had an estimated population of 17,093,000 as of January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs-counter_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs-counter-140">[137]</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population" title="List of European countries by population">most populous country in Europe</a> by size, except for very small city countries like <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>, etc. and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">63rd most populous country</a> in the world. Between 1900 and 1950, the country's population almost doubled from 5.1 to 10 million. From 1950 to 2000, the population further increased, to 15.9&#160;million, though this represented a lower rate of <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[138]</a></sup> The estimated growth rate in 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is 0.44%.<sup id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-142">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> in the Netherlands is 1.78 children per woman (2013 est.<sup id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-142">[139]</a></sup>), which is high compared with many other European countries, but <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">below the rate of 2.1 children per woman required for natural population replacement</a>. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> is high in the Netherlands: 83.21 years for newborn girls and 78.93 for boys (2013 est.<sup id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-142">[139]</a></sup>). The country has a <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> rate of 1.99 migrants per 1,000 inhabitants per year.<sup id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_142-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-142">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of the population of the Netherlands is ethnically <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>. According to a 2005 estimate, the population was 80.9% Dutch, 2.4% <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a>, 2.4% <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a>, 2.2% <a href="/wiki/Turkish-Dutch" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish-Dutch">Turkish</a>, 2.0% <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_people" title="Surinamese people">Surinamese</a>, 1.9% <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a>, 0.8% <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Antillean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruban</a>, and 7.4% others.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[140]</a></sup> Some 150,000 to 200,000 people living in the Netherlands are <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a>, mostly concentrated in and around <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, now constituting almost 10% of the population of these cities.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> are the tallest people in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Science_2015-04-07_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Science_2015-04-07-146">[143]</a></sup> with an average <a href="/wiki/Human_height" title="Human height">height</a> of 1.81 metres (5&#160;ft 11.3&#160;in) for adult males and 1.67 metres (5&#160;ft 5.7&#160;in) for adult females in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[144]</a></sup> People in the south are on average about 2&#160;cm (0.8 inches) shorter than those in the north.</p>
<p>Dutch people, or <a href="/wiki/Dutch_diaspora" title="Dutch diaspora">descendants of Dutch people</a>, are also found in migrant communities worldwide, notably in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="The United States">the United States</a>. According to the 2006 US Census, more than 5&#160;million Americans claim total or partial <a href="/wiki/Dutch_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch American">Dutch</a> ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[145]</a></sup> There are close to 3&#160;million Dutch-descended <a href="/wiki/Afrikaner" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrikaner">Afrikaners</a> living in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[146]</a></sup> In 1940, there were 290,000 Europeans and Eurasians in Indonesia,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[147]</a></sup> but most have since left the country.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[148]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, in 2010 there were 1.8 million foreign-born residents in the Netherlands, corresponding to 11.1% of the total population. Of these, 1.4 million (8.5%) were born outside the EU and 0.428 million (2.6%) were born in another EU Member State.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands is the 24th <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">most densely populated</a> country in the world, with 408.53 inhabitants per square kilometre (1,058/sq&#160;mi) or – if only the land area is counted (33,883&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, 13,082&#160;sq&#160;mi) – 500.89 inhabitants per square kilometre (1,297/sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[150]</a></sup> When the land area of the provinces only is counted (33,718&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, 13,019&#160;sq&#160;mi), a number of 500 inhabitants per square kilometre (1,295/sq&#160;mi) was reached in the first half of 2014. The <a href="/wiki/Randstad" title="Randstad">Randstad</a> is the country's largest <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a> located in the west of the country and contains the four largest cities: Amsterdam in the province <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> in the province <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Utrecht (city)">Utrecht</a> in the province <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(province)" title="Utrecht (province)">Utrecht</a>. The Randstad has a population of 7&#160;million inhabitants and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of metropolitan areas in Europe by population">6th largest</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> in Europe. According to Dutch Central Statistics Bureau, in 2015, 28 percent of Dutch population had a spendable income above 40 thousand EUR.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p><br /></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Netherlands" title="Languages of the Netherlands">Languages of the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Foreign_languages_Netherlands,_2005.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png/350px-Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png" width="350" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png/525px-Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png/700px-Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png 2x" data-file-width="712" data-file-height="424" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Foreign_languages_Netherlands,_2005.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Knowledge of foreign languages in the Netherlands, in percent of the population over 15, 2006. Data taken from an EU survey. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/public_opinion/archives/ebs/ebs_243_en.pdf">ebs_243_en.pdf</a> (europa.eu)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The official language is <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, which is spoken by the vast majority of the inhabitants. Besides Dutch, <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">West Frisian</a> is recognised as a second official language in the northern province of <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a> (<i>Fryslân</i> in West Frisian).<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup> West Frisian has a formal status for government correspondence in that province. In the European part of the Netherlands two other regional languages are recognised under the <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first of these regional languages is <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Low_Saxon" title="Dutch Low Saxon">Low Saxon</a> (<i>Nedersaksisch</i> in Dutch) is recognised. Low Saxon consists of several dialects spoken in the north and east, like <a href="/wiki/Twents" class="mw-redirect" title="Twents">Twents</a> in the region of <a href="/wiki/Twente" title="Twente">Twente</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drents" class="mw-redirect" title="Drents">Drents</a> in the province of <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a>. Secondly, <a href="/wiki/Limburgish" class="mw-redirect" title="Limburgish">Limburgish</a> is also recognised as a regional language. It consists of Dutch varieties of <a href="/wiki/Meuse-Rhenish" title="Meuse-Rhenish">Meuse-Rhenish</a> <a href="/wiki/Franconian_languages" title="Franconian languages">Franconian languages</a> and is spoken in the south-eastern province of <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-international2000_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international2000-70">[68]</a></sup> The dialects most spoken in the Netherlands are the <a href="/wiki/Brabantian" class="mw-redirect" title="Brabantian">Brabantian</a>-<a href="/wiki/Hollandic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hollandic">Hollandic</a> dialects.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_language" title="Ripuarian language">Ripuarian language</a>, which is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Kerkrade" title="Kerkrade">Kerkrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vaals" title="Vaals">Vaals</a> in the form of, respectively, the <a href="/wiki/Kerkrade_dialect" title="Kerkrade dialect">Kerkrade dialect</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vaals_dialect" title="Vaals dialect">Vaals dialect</a><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup> is not recognised as a regional language of the Netherlands.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/English_in_the_Netherlands" title="English in the Netherlands">English</a> has a formal status in the special municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>. It is widely spoken on these islands. <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">Papiamento</a> has a formal status in the special municipality of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">Yiddish</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a> were recognised in 1996 as non-territorial languages.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Netherlands has a tradition of learning foreign languages, formalised in Dutch education laws. Some 90% of the total population indicate <a href="/wiki/English_in_the_Netherlands" title="English in the Netherlands">they are able to converse in English</a>, 70% in German, and 29% in French.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[160]</a></sup> English is a mandatory course in all secondary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-xyz_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xyz-164">[161]</a></sup> In most lower level secondary school educations (<i><a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_middelbaar_beroepsonderwijs" title="Voorbereidend middelbaar beroepsonderwijs">vmbo</a></i>), one additional modern foreign language is mandatory during the first two years.<sup id="cite_ref-Schedule_of_the_Central_Exams_of_2009_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schedule_of_the_Central_Exams_of_2009-165">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>In higher level secondary schools (<i><a href="/wiki/Hoger_algemeen_voortgezet_onderwijs" title="Hoger algemeen voortgezet onderwijs">havo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_wetenschappelijk_onderwijs" title="Voorbereidend wetenschappelijk onderwijs">vwo</a></i>), two additional modern foreign languages are mandatory during the first three years. Only during the last three years in <i>vwo</i> one foreign language is mandatory. Besides English, the standard modern languages are French and German, although schools can replace one of these modern languages with Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, or Russian.<sup id="cite_ref-Schedule_of_the_Central_Exams_of_2009_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schedule_of_the_Central_Exams_of_2009-165">[162]</a></sup> Additionally, schools in Friesland teach and have exams in <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">Frisian</a>, and schools across the country teach and have exams in classical Greek and Latin for secondary school (called gymnasium or vwo+).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Netherlands" title="Religion in the Netherlands">Religion in the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden">
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Orange"></div>

<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 29.052685673192px; border-left-color:DarkOrchid"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid"></div>

<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:89.940525156637px 43.711576665093px 0 0; border-top-color:Honeydew"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Honeydew"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;left:0;top:0"><img alt="Circle frame.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/200px-Circle_frame.svg.png" width="200" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/300px-Circle_frame.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/400px-Circle_frame.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200" /></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religions in the Netherlands (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-BerntsA_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BerntsA-166">[163]</a></sup></p>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Honeydew; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">No affiliation</a> (67.8%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkOrchid; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> (11.7%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a> (8.6%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Turquoise; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian denominations (4.2%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Netherlands" title="Islam in the Netherlands">Islam</a> (5.8%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (2.0%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Historically, the Netherlands was a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> society. From the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, the Dutch population became divided into about two-thirds <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a>) and one-third <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> believers.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[nb 4]</a></sup> This began to change gradually in the 20th century<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[nb 5]</a></sup> as there has been a steep decline in religious adherence, which continues. There was a <a href="/wiki/Pillarisation" title="Pillarisation">strong religious difference</a> between the Roman Catholic south and the Reformed north, remains of which are still in evidence. The Netherlands is currently one of the most <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a> countries in the world. About 39% of the population is religiously affiliated and in 2010 fewer than 5.6% visited religious services regularly (once or more per month). In spite of an overall decline in religiosity, a countervailing trend is the religious revival in the Protestant <a href="/wiki/Bible_Belt_(Netherlands)" title="Bible Belt (Netherlands)">Bible Belt</a>, and the growth of Muslim and Hindu communities.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Religion in the Netherlands is generally considered a personal matter and is not supposed to be propagated in public.<sup id="cite_ref-Becker.2C_Jos_and_Joep_de_Hart_2006_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Becker.2C_Jos_and_Joep_de_Hart_2006-171">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[168]</a></sup> The Dutch constitution guarantees freedom of education, which means that all schools that adhere to general quality criteria receive the same government funding. This includes schools based on religious principles by religious groups (especially Roman Catholic and various Protestant). Three political parties in the Dutch parliament (<a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Appeal" title="Christian Democratic Appeal">CDA</a>, <a href="/wiki/ChristianUnion" class="mw-redirect" title="ChristianUnion">ChristianUnion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Political_Party" title="Reformed Political Party">SGP</a>) are based upon the Christian belief. Several Christian religious holidays are national holidays (Christmas, Easter, <a href="/wiki/Pentecost" title="Pentecost">Pentecost</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ascension_of_Jesus" title="Ascension of Jesus">Ascension of Jesus</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is currently the largest religion in the Netherlands, accounting for about one-third of the population. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in the Netherlands">Roman Catholicism</a> is the largest Christian religious grouping with around four million registered adherents (23.7% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-SILA_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SILA-175">[170]</a></sup> The provinces of <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg</a> have historically been strongly Roman Catholic, and their people still largely consider the Catholic Church as a base for their <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Christian" title="Cultural Christian">cultural identity</a>. Protestantism in the Netherlands consists of a number of churches within various traditions. The largest of these is the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a> (PKN) (10.2% of the population), a <a href="/wiki/United_and_uniting_churches" title="United and uniting churches">United</a> church which is <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a> in orientation.<sup id="cite_ref-CBS_2009_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_2009-176">[171]</a></sup> It was formed in 2004 as a merger of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Churches_in_the_Netherlands" title="Reformed Churches in the Netherlands">Reformed Churches in the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in the Kingdom of the Netherlands">a smaller Lutheran Church</a>. Several orthodox Reformed and liberal churches did not merge into the PKN. Although in the Netherlands as a whole Christianity has become a minority, the Netherlands contains a <a href="/wiki/Bible_Belt_(Netherlands)" title="Bible Belt (Netherlands)">Bible Belt</a> from <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a> to the northern parts of the province <a href="/wiki/Overijssel" title="Overijssel">Overijssel</a>, in which Protestant (particularly Reformed) beliefs remain strong, and even has majorities in municipal councils. The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Royal Family">Dutch Royal Family</a> has historically been Reformed.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the second largest religion in the state. In 2012, there were about 825,000 <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Netherlands" title="Islam in the Netherlands">Muslims</a> in the Netherlands (5% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-CBS2_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS2-177">[172]</a></sup> Muslim numbers increased from the 1960 as a consequence of large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Netherlands#Im-_and_Emigration" title="Demographics of the Netherlands">migrant workers</a>. This included migrants from former <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch colonies</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Surinam" class="mw-redirect" title="Surinam">Surinam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, but mainly migrant workers from <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. During the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Muslim_refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim refugees">Muslim refugees</a> arrived from countries like <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other religions account for some 6% of the Dutch people. Hinduism is a minority religion in the Netherlands, with around 215,000 adherents (slightly over 1% of the population). Most of these are <a href="/wiki/Indo-Surinamese" title="Indo-Surinamese">Indo-Surinamese</a>. There are also sizable populations of Hindu immigrants from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, and some Western adherents of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_West" title="Hinduism in the West">Hinduism-oriented new religious movements</a> such as <a href="/wiki/International_Society_for_Krishna_Consciousness" title="International Society for Krishna Consciousness">Hare Krishnas</a>. The Netherlands has an estimated 250,000 <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_the_Netherlands" title="Buddhism in the Netherlands">Buddhists</a> or people strongly attracted to this religion, mainly ethnic Dutch people. There are about 45,000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Jews</a> in the Netherlands.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Netherlands" title="Education in the Netherlands">Education in the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>Education in the Netherlands is compulsory between the ages of 5 and 16 when HAVO, VWO or MBO level 2 or higher completed or 18.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>All children in the Netherlands usually attend elementary school from (on average) ages 4 to 12. It comprises eight grades, the first of which is facultative. Based on an aptitude test, the 8th grade teacher's recommendation and the opinion of the pupil's parents or caretakers, a choice is made for one of the three main streams of secondary education (after completing a particular stream, a pupil may still continue in the penultimate year of the next stream):</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_middelbaar_beroepsonderwijs" title="Voorbereidend middelbaar beroepsonderwijs">vmbo</a> has 4 grades and is subdivided over several levels. Successfully completing the vmbo results in a low-level vocational degree that grants access to the mbo.
<ul>
<li>MBO ("middle-level applied education"). This form of education primarily focuses on teaching a practical trade, or a vocational degree. With the MBO certification, a student can apply for the HBO.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Hoger_algemeen_voortgezet_onderwijs" title="Hoger algemeen voortgezet onderwijs">havo</a> has 5 grades and allows for admission to the hbo.
<ul>
<li>HBO ("higher professional education"), are <a href="/wiki/Vocational_university" title="Vocational university">universities of professional education</a> (or applied sciences) that award professional bachelor's degrees; similar to polytechnic degrees. A HBO degrees gives access to the university system.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_wetenschappelijk_onderwijs" title="Voorbereidend wetenschappelijk onderwijs">vwo</a> (comprising <a href="/wiki/Atheneum_(school)" title="Atheneum (school)">atheneum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasium</a>) has 6 grades and prepares for studying at a (research) university.
<ul>
<li>Universities offer of a three-year bachelor's degree, followed by a one-, two- or three year master's degree, which in turn can be followed by a four-year <a href="/wiki/Doctoral_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctoral degree">doctoral degree</a> program. Doctoral candidates in the Netherlands are generally non-tenured employees of a university.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_Netherlands" title="Healthcare in the Netherlands">Healthcare in the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_(1632-1723)._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg/220px-Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg" width="220" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg/330px-Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg/440px-Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2148" data-file-height="2547" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_(1632-1723)._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Antonie_van_Leeuwenhoek" title="Antonie van Leeuwenhoek">Antonie van Leeuwenhoek</a> (1632–1723) by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Verkolje" title="Jan Verkolje">Jan Verkolje</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UMC_Utrecht.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/UMC_Utrecht.jpg/220px-UMC_Utrecht.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/UMC_Utrecht.jpg/330px-UMC_Utrecht.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/UMC_Utrecht.jpg/440px-UMC_Utrecht.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UMC_Utrecht.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/University_Medical_Center_Utrecht" title="University Medical Center Utrecht">University Medical Center Utrecht</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2015 the Netherlands has maintained its number one position at the top of the annual <a href="/wiki/Euro_health_consumer_index" title="Euro health consumer index">Euro health consumer index</a> (EHCI), which compares healthcare systems in Europe, scoring 916 of a maximum 1,000 points. The Netherlands has been in the top three countries in each report published since 2005. On 48 indicators such as patient rights and information, accessibility, prevention and outcomes, the Netherlands secured its top position among 37 European countries for the sixth year in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[175]</a></sup> The Netherlands was ranked first in a study in 2009 comparing the <a href="/wiki/Health_care_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care system">health care systems</a> of the United States, Australia, Canada, Germany and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ever since a major reform of the health care system in 2006, the Dutch system received more points in the Index each year. According to the HCP (<a href="/wiki/Health_Consumer_Powerhouse" title="Health Consumer Powerhouse">Health Consumer Powerhouse</a>), the Netherlands has 'a chaos system', meaning patients have a great degree of freedom from where to buy their health insurance, to where they get their healthcare service. But the difference between the Netherlands and other countries is that the chaos is managed. Healthcare decisions are being made in a dialogue between the patients and healthcare professionals.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>Health insurance in the Netherlands is mandatory. Healthcare in the Netherlands is covered by two statutory forms of insurance:</p>
<ul>
<li>Zorgverzekeringswet (Zvw), often called "basic insurance", covers common medical care.</li>
<li>Algemene Wet Bijzondere Ziektekosten (AWBZ) covers long-term nursing and care. While Dutch residents are automatically insured by the government for AWBZ, everyone has to take out their own basic healthcare insurance (basisverzekering), except those under 18 who are automatically covered under their parents' premium. If you don't take out insurance, you risk a fine. Insurers have to offer a universal package for everyone over the age of 18 years, regardless of age or state of health – it's illegal to refuse an application or impose special conditions. In contrast to many other European systems, the Dutch government is responsible for the accessibility and quality of the healthcare system in the Netherlands, but not in charge of its management.</li>
</ul>
<p>Healthcare in the Netherlands can be divided in several ways: three echelons, in somatic and mental health care and in 'cure' (short term) and 'care' (long term). Home doctors (<i>huisartsen</i>, comparable to <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">General Practitioners</a>) form the largest part of the first echelon. Being referenced by a member of the first echelon is mandatory for access to the second and third echelon.<sup id="cite_ref-Boot_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boot-184">[179]</a></sup> The health care system is in comparison to other Western countries quite effective but not the most cost-effective.<sup id="cite_ref-BCG_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BCG-185">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>Healthcare in the Netherlands is financed by a dual system that came into effect in January 2006. Long-term treatments, especially those that involve semi-permanent hospitalization, and also disability costs such as wheelchairs, are covered by a state-controlled mandatory insurance. This is laid down in the <i><a href="/wiki/AWBZ" title="AWBZ">Algemene Wet Bijzondere Ziektekosten</a></i> ("General Law on Exceptional Healthcare Costs") which first came into effect in 1968. In 2009 this insurance covered 27% of all health care expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>For all regular (short-term) medical treatment, there is a system of obligatory <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>, with private health insurance companies. These insurance companies are obliged to provide a package with a defined set of insured treatments.<sup id="cite_ref-minvws.nl_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minvws.nl-187">[182]</a></sup> This insurance covers 41% of all health care expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-statline.cbs.nl_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statline.cbs.nl-188">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other sources of health care payment are taxes (14%), out of pocket payments (9%), additional optional health insurance packages (4%) and a range of other sources (4%).<sup id="cite_ref-statline.cbs.nl_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statline.cbs.nl-188">[183]</a></sup> Affordability is guaranteed through a system of income-related allowances and individual and employer-paid income-related premiums.</p>
<p>A key feature of the Dutch system is that premiums may not be related to health status or age. Risk variances between private health insurance companies due to the different risks presented by individual policy holders are compensated through <a href="/wiki/Risk_equalization" title="Risk equalization">risk equalization</a> and a common <a href="/wiki/Risk_pool" title="Risk pool">risk pool</a>. Funding for all short-term health care is 50% from employers, 45% from the insured person and 5% by the government. Children under 18 are covered for free. Those on low incomes receive compensation to help them pay their insurance. Premiums paid by the insured are about 100&#160;€ per month (about US$127 in Aug. 2010 and in 2012 €150 or US$196,) with variation of about 5% between the various competing insurers, and deductible a year €220 US$288.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Netherlands" title="Culture of the Netherlands">Culture of the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hollande04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hollande04.jpg/320px-Hollande04.jpg" width="320" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hollande04.jpg/480px-Hollande04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hollande04.jpg/640px-Hollande04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="792" data-file-height="278" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hollande04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Symbols and icons of Dutch culture</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art.2C_philosophy_and_literature">Art, philosophy and literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Art, philosophy and literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_art" title="Dutch art">Dutch art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch literature">Dutch literature</a></div>
<p>The Netherlands has had many well-known painters.
