The 17th century, in which the Dutch Republic was prosperous, was the age of the "Dutch Masters", such as <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt_Harmenszoon_van_Rijn" class="mw-redirect" title="Rembrandt Harmenszoon van Rijn">Rembrandt van Rijn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Vermeer" title="Johannes Vermeer">Johannes Vermeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Steen" title="Jan Steen">Jan Steen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacob_van_Ruisdael" title="Jacob van Ruisdael">Jacob van Ruisdael</a> and many others. Famous Dutch painters of the 19th and 20th century were <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Vincent van Gogh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piet_Mondrian" title="Piet Mondrian">Piet Mondriaan</a>. <a href="/wiki/M._C._Escher" title="M. C. Escher">M. C. Escher</a> is a well-known graphics artist. <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Kooning" title="Willem de Kooning">Willem de Kooning</a> was born and trained in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, although he is considered to have reached acclaim as an American artist.</p>
<p>The Netherlands is the country of philosophers <a href="/wiki/Erasmus" title="Erasmus">Erasmus of Rotterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baruch_Spinoza" title="Baruch Spinoza">Spinoza</a>. All of <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Descartes" title="René Descartes">Descartes</a>' major work was done in the Netherlands. The Dutch scientist <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens" title="Christiaan Huygens">Christiaan Huygens</a> (1629–1695) discovered <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>'s moon <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>, argued that light travelled as waves, invented the <a href="/wiki/Pendulum_clock" title="Pendulum clock">pendulum clock</a> and was the first physicist to use mathematical formulae. <a href="/wiki/Antonie_van_Leeuwenhoek" title="Antonie van Leeuwenhoek">Antonie van Leeuwenhoek</a> was the first to observe and describe <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">single-celled organisms</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Microscope" title="Microscope">microscope</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Holbein-erasmus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/150px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg" width="150" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/225px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/300px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="809" data-file-height="1145" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Holbein-erasmus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Erasmus" title="Erasmus">Erasmus</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>, literature flourished as well, with <a href="/wiki/Joost_van_den_Vondel" title="Joost van den Vondel">Joost van den Vondel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Corneliszoon_Hooft" title="Pieter Corneliszoon Hooft">P. C. Hooft</a> as the two most famous writers. In the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Multatuli" title="Multatuli">Multatuli</a> wrote about the poor treatment of the natives in the Dutch colony, the current Indonesia. Important 20th century authors include <a href="/wiki/Godfried_Bomans" title="Godfried Bomans">Godfried Bomans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Mulisch" title="Harry Mulisch">Harry Mulisch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Wolkers" title="Jan Wolkers">Jan Wolkers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Vestdijk" title="Simon Vestdijk">Simon Vestdijk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hella_S._Haasse" class="mw-redirect" title="Hella S. Haasse">Hella S. Haasse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cees_Nooteboom" title="Cees Nooteboom">Cees Nooteboom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerard_van_het_Reve" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerard van het Reve">Gerard (van het) Reve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willem_Frederik_Hermans" title="Willem Frederik Hermans">Willem Frederik Hermans</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank" title="Anne Frank">Anne Frank</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Diary_of_a_Young_Girl" title="The Diary of a Young Girl"><i>Diary of a Young Girl</i></a> was published after she died in the Holocaust and translated from Dutch to all major languages.</p>
<p>The traditional Dutch architecture is especially valuated in Amsterdam, <a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leiden" title="Leiden">Leiden</a>, with 17 and 18th century buildings along the canals. Smaller village architecture with wooden houses is found in <a href="/wiki/Zaandam" title="Zaandam">Zaandam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marken" title="Marken">Marken</a>. Replicas of Dutch buildings can be found in <a href="/wiki/Huis_Ten_Bosch_(theme_park)" title="Huis Ten Bosch (theme park)">Huis Ten Bosch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>, Japan. A similar Holland Village is being built in <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a>, China. <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">Windmills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tulip" title="Tulip">tulips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clog_(shoe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Clog (shoe)">wooden shoes</a>, cheese, <a href="/wiki/Delftware" title="Delftware">Delftware</a> pottery, and <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> are among the items associated with the Netherlands by tourists.</p>
<p>The Netherlands has a long history of social tolerance and today is regarded as a liberal country, considering <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">its drug policy</a> and its legalisation of <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a>. On 1 April 2001, the Netherlands became the first nation to legalise <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_Netherlands" title="Same-sex marriage in the Netherlands">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_value_system_and_etiquette">Dutch value system and etiquette</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Dutch value system and etiquette">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_(14823067801).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_%2814823067801%29.jpg/220px-PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_%2814823067801%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_%2814823067801%29.jpg/330px-PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_%2814823067801%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_%2814823067801%29.jpg/440px-PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_%2814823067801%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4912" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PvdAboot_op_de_Amsterdam_Gay_Parade_2014_(14823067801).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Gay_Pride" title="Amsterdam Gay Pride">Amsterdam Gay Pride</a> 2004.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Dutch have a <a href="/wiki/Dutch_customs_and_etiquette" title="Dutch customs and etiquette">code of etiquette</a> which governs social behaviour and is considered important. Because of the international position of the Netherlands, many books have been written on the subject. Some customs may not be true in all regions and they are never absolute. In addition to those specific to the Dutch, many general points of <a href="/wiki/Etiquette_in_Europe" title="Etiquette in Europe">European etiquette</a> apply to the Dutch as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-190">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dutch society is <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarian</a>, individualistic and modern. The people tend to view themselves as modest, independent and self-reliant. They value ability over dependency. The Dutch have an aversion to the non-essential.<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-190">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ostentatious behaviour is to be avoided. Accumulating money is fine, but public spending of large amounts of money is considered something of a <a href="/wiki/Vice" title="Vice">vice</a> and associated with being a show-off. A high lifestyle is considered wasteful and suspect with most people. The Dutch are proud of their <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">cultural heritage</a>, rich history in art and involvement in <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-190">[185]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg/220px-Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg/330px-Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg/440px-Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queensday_2011_Amsterdam_26.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dutch people in orange celebrating <a href="/wiki/Koningsdag" title="Koningsdag">King's Day</a> in Amsterdam.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dutch manners are open and direct with a no-nonsense attitude; informality combined with adherence to basic behaviour. According to a humorous source on Dutch culture, "Their directness gives many the impression that they are rude and crude—attributes they prefer to call 'openness.'"<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_190-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-190">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>A well known more serious source on Dutch etiquette is "Dealing with the Dutch" from Jacob Vossestein: "Dutch egalitarianism is the idea that people are equal, especially from a moral point of view, and accordingly, causes the somewhat ambiguous stance the Dutch have towards hierarchy and status."<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[186]</a></sup> As always, manners differ between groups. Asking about basic rules will not be considered impolite. "What may strike you as being blatantly blunt topics and comments are no more embarrassing or unusual to the Dutch than discussing the weather."<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_190-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-190">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of the Dutch are <a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">irreligious</a> and religion is in the Netherlands generally considered as a very personal matter which is not supposed to be propagated in public.<sup id="cite_ref-Becker.2C_Jos_and_Joep_de_Hart_2006_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Becker.2C_Jos_and_Joep_de_Hart_2006-171">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_people_and_ecology">Dutch people and ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Dutch people and ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Netherlands has the <a href="/wiki/Reputation" title="Reputation">reputation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">leader</a> <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Environmental_science" title="Environmental science">environmental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">population management</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[187]</a></sup> In 2015, Amsterdam and Rotterdam were, respectively, at the 4th and the 5th position on the <a href="/wiki/Arcadis_NV" class="mw-redirect" title="Arcadis NV">Arcadis Sustainable Cities Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">Sustainability</a> is a concept important for the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>. The goal of the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Netherlands" title="Politics of the Netherlands">Dutch Government</a> is to have a <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable</a>, reliable and affordable energy system, by 2050, in which <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth's atmosphere">CO2 emissions</a> have been halved and 40 percent of <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> is derived from <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable sources</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-195">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> is investing billions of euros in <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">CO2 reduction</a>. The Kingdom also encourage Dutch <a href="/wiki/Companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Companies">companies</a> to build <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_business" title="Sustainable business">sustainable business</a>/<a href="/wiki/Project" title="Project">projects</a>/<a href="/wiki/Facility_management" title="Facility management">facilities</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">financial aids</a> from the state to the companies or <a href="/wiki/Individual" title="Individual">individuals</a> who are active in making the <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> more <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-195">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Netherlands" title="Music of the Netherlands">Music of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_former_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Music of the former Netherlands Antilles">Music of the former Netherlands Antilles</a></div>
<p>The Netherlands has multiple <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a> traditions. Traditional Dutch music is a genre known as "<a href="/wiki/Levenslied" title="Levenslied">Levenslied</a>", meaning <i>Song of life</i>, to an extent comparable to a French <a href="/wiki/Chanson" title="Chanson">Chanson</a> or a German <a href="/wiki/Schlager_music" title="Schlager music">Schlager</a>. These songs typically have a simple melody and rhythm, and a straightforward structure of couplets and refrains. Themes can be light, but are often sentimental and include <a href="/wiki/Love" title="Love">love</a>, <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">death</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loneliness" title="Loneliness">loneliness</a>. Traditional musical instruments such as the <a href="/wiki/Accordion" title="Accordion">accordion</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Barrel_organ" title="Barrel organ">barrel organ</a> are a staple of levenslied music, though in recent years many artists also use synthesizers and guitars. Artists in this genre include <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smit_(singer)" title="Jan Smit (singer)">Jan Smit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frans_Bauer" title="Frans Bauer">Frans Bauer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Hazes" title="André Hazes">André Hazes</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG/170px-Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG/255px-Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG/340px-Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pop singer <a href="/wiki/Anouk_(singer)" title="Anouk (singer)">Anouk</a> at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Festival_Mundial&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Festival Mundial (page does not exist)">Festival Mundial</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Festival_Mundial" class="extiw" title="nl:Festival Mundial">nl</a>)</span><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[191]</a></sup> in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Contemporary Dutch <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop music</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nederpop" title="Nederpop">Nederpop</a>) originated in the 1960s, heavily influenced by popular music from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>. In the 1960s and 1970s the lyrics were mostly in English, and some tracks were instrumental. Bands such as <a href="/wiki/Shocking_Blue" title="Shocking Blue">Shocking Blue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Earring" title="Golden Earring">Golden Earring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tee_Set" title="Tee Set">Tee Set</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Baker_Selection" title="George Baker Selection">George Baker Selection</a> and <a href="/wiki/Focus_(band)" title="Focus (band)">Focus</a> enjoyed international success. As of the 1980s, more and more pop musicians started working in the Dutch language, partly inspired by the huge success of the band <a href="/wiki/Doe_Maar" title="Doe Maar">Doe Maar</a>. Today Dutch rock and pop music thrives in both languages, with some artists recording in both.</p>
<p>Current <a href="/wiki/Symphonic_metal" title="Symphonic metal">symphonic metal</a> bands <a href="/wiki/Epica_(band)" title="Epica (band)">Epica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delain" title="Delain">Delain</a>, <a href="/wiki/ReVamp" title="ReVamp">ReVamp</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Gathering_(band)" title="The Gathering (band)">The Gathering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asrai" title="Asrai">Asrai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">Autumn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayreon" title="Ayreon">Ayreon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Within_Temptation" title="Within Temptation">Within Temptation</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> / pop singer <a href="/wiki/Caro_Emerald" title="Caro Emerald">Caro Emerald</a> are having international success. Also metalbands like <a href="/wiki/Hail_of_Bullets" title="Hail of Bullets">Hail of Bullets</a>, <a href="/wiki/God_Dethroned" title="God Dethroned">God Dethroned</a>, <a href="/wiki/Izegrim" title="Izegrim">Izegrim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asphyx" title="Asphyx">Asphyx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textures_(band)" title="Textures (band)">Textures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Present_Danger" title="Present Danger">Present Danger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heidevolk" title="Heidevolk">Heidevolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slechtvalk" title="Slechtvalk">Slechtvalk</a> are popular guests at the biggest <a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_festivals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Metal festivals (page does not exist)">metal festivals</a> in Europe. Contemporary local heroes include pop singer <a href="/wiki/Anouk_(singer)" title="Anouk (singer)">Anouk</a>, country pop singer <a href="/wiki/Ilse_DeLange" title="Ilse DeLange">Ilse DeLange</a>, in <a href="/wiki/South_Guelderish" title="South Guelderish">South Guelderish</a> dialect singing folk band <a href="/wiki/Rowwen_H%C3%A8ze" title="Rowwen Hèze">Rowwen Hèze</a>, rock band <a href="/wiki/BL%C3%98F" title="BLØF">BLØF</a> and Dutch language duo <a href="/wiki/Nick_%26_Simon" title="Nick &amp; Simon">Nick &amp; Simon</a>.</p>
<p>Early 1990s Dutch and <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgian</a> <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house music</a> came together in <a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">Eurodance</a> project <a href="/wiki/2_Unlimited" title="2 Unlimited">2 Unlimited</a>. Selling 18 million records,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[192]</a></sup> the two singers in the band are the most successful Dutch music artists to this day. Tracks like "<a href="/wiki/Get_Ready_for_This" title="Get Ready for This">Get Ready for This</a>" are still popular themes of U.S. sports events, like the <a href="/wiki/NHL" class="mw-redirect" title="NHL">NHL</a>. In the mid 1990s Dutch language <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">rap and hip hop</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Dutch_hip_hop" title="Dutch hip hop">Nederhop</a></i>) also came to fruition and has become popular in the Netherlands and Belgium. Artists with North African, Caribbean or Middle Eastern origins have strongly influenced this genre.</p>
<p>Since the 1990s Dutch <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">electronic dance music (EDM)</a> conquered the world in many forms, from <a href="/wiki/Trance" title="Trance">trance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabber" title="Gabber">gabber</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hardstyle" title="Hardstyle">hardstyle</a>. Some of the world's best dance music DJs hail from the Netherlands, including <a href="/wiki/Armin_van_Buuren" title="Armin van Buuren">Armin van Buuren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ti%C3%ABsto" title="Tiësto">Tiësto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hardwell" title="Hardwell">Hardwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Garrix" title="Martin Garrix">Martin Garrix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dash_Berlin" title="Dash Berlin">Dash Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Romero" title="Nicky Romero">Nicky Romero</a>, <a href="/wiki/W%26W" title="W&amp;W">W&amp;W</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afrojack" title="Afrojack">Afrojack</a>; the first four of which have been ranked as best in the world by <a href="/wiki/DJ_Mag_Top_100_DJs" class="mw-redirect" title="DJ Mag Top 100 DJs">DJ Mag Top 100 DJs</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_dance_event" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam dance event">Amsterdam dance event</a> (ADE) is the world's leading electronic music conference and the biggest club festival for the many electronic subgenres on the planet.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[194]</a></sup> These DJs also contribute to the world's mainstream pop music, as they frequently collaborate and produce for high profile international artists.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Sweelinck" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Sweelinck">Jan Sweelinck</a> ranks as the Dutch most famous composer, with <a href="/wiki/Louis_Andriessen" title="Louis Andriessen">Louis Andriessen</a> amongst the best known living Dutch classical composers. <a href="/wiki/Ton_Koopman" title="Ton Koopman">Ton Koopman</a> is a Dutch conductor, organist and harpsichordist. He is also professor at the Royal Conservatory of The Hague. Notable violinists are <a href="/wiki/Janine_Jansen" title="Janine Jansen">Janine Jansen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Rieu" title="André Rieu">André Rieu</a>. The latter, together with his <a href="/wiki/Johann_Strauss_Orchestra" title="Johann Strauss Orchestra">Johann Strauss Orchestra</a>, has taken classical and <a href="/wiki/Waltz_(music)" title="Waltz (music)">waltz music</a> on worldwide concert tours, the size and revenue of which are otherwise only seen from the world's biggest rock and pop music acts. The most famous Dutch classical composition is "Canto Ostinato" by Simeon ten Holt. A minimalistic composition for multiple instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[197]</a></sup> Acclaimed harpist <a href="/wiki/Lavinia_Meijer" title="Lavinia Meijer">Lavinia Meijer</a> in 2012 released an album with works from <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a> that she transcribed for harp, with approval of Glass himself.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[198]</a></sup><br />
The <a href="/wiki/Concertgebouw" title="Concertgebouw">Concertgebouw</a> (completed in 1888) in Amsterdam is home to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Concertgebouw_Orchestra" title="Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra">Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra</a>, considered one of the world's finest orchestras.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[199]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television">Film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_Netherlands" title="Cinema of the Netherlands">Cinema of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Television_in_the_Netherlands" title="Television in the Netherlands">Television in the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Voice_Of_.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/The_Voice_Of_.jpg/220px-The_Voice_Of_.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/The_Voice_Of_.jpg/330px-The_Voice_Of_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/56/The_Voice_Of_.jpg 2x" data-file-width="336" data-file-height="336" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Voice_Of_.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(TV_series)" title="The Voice (TV series)">The Voice franchise</a> originated in the Netherlands</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some Dutch films – mainly by director <a href="/wiki/Paul_Verhoeven" title="Paul Verhoeven">Paul Verhoeven</a> – have received international distribution and recognition, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Delight_(1973_film)" title="Turkish Delight (1973 film)">Turkish Delight</a></i> ("<i>Turks Fruit</i>") (1973), <i><a href="/wiki/Soldier_of_Orange" title="Soldier of Orange">Soldier of Orange</a></i> ("<i>Soldaat van Oranje</i>") (1975), <i><a href="/wiki/Spetters" title="Spetters">Spetters</a></i> (1980) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fourth_Man_(1983_film)" title="The Fourth Man (1983 film)">The Fourth Man</a></i> ("<i>De Vierde Man</i>") (1983). Verhoeven then went on to direct big <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood</a> movies like <i><a href="/wiki/RoboCop" title="RoboCop">RoboCop</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Recall_(1990_film)" title="Total Recall (1990 film)">Total Recall (1990)</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Basic_Instinct" title="Basic Instinct">Basic Instinct</a></i>, and returned with Dutch film <a href="/wiki/Black_Book_(film)" title="Black Book (film)">Black Book</a> in 2006.</p>
<p>Other well-known Dutch film directors are <a href="/wiki/Jan_de_Bont" title="Jan de Bont">Jan de Bont</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Speed_(1994_film)" title="Speed (1994 film)">Speed</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Anton_Corbijn" title="Anton Corbijn">Anton Corbijn</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/A_Most_Wanted_Man_(film)" title="A Most Wanted Man (film)">A Most wanted Man</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Dick_Maas" title="Dick Maas">Dick Maas</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/De_Lift" title="De Lift">De Lift</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Fons_Rademakers" title="Fons Rademakers">Fons Rademakers</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Assault_(film)" title="The Assault (film)">The Assault</a></i>), documentary maker <a href="/wiki/Bert_Haanstra" title="Bert Haanstra">Bert Haanstra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joris_Ivens" title="Joris Ivens">Joris Ivens</a>. Film director <a href="/wiki/Theo_van_Gogh_(film_director)" title="Theo van Gogh (film director)">Theo van Gogh</a> achieved international notoriety in 2004 when he was murdered in the streets of <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> after directing the short film <a href="/wiki/Submission_(2004_film)" title="Submission (2004 film)">Submission</a>.</p>
<p>Internationally successful Dutch actors include <a href="/wiki/Famke_Janssen" title="Famke Janssen">Famke Janssen</a> (<a href="/wiki/X-Men_(film_series)" title="X-Men (film series)"><i>X-Men</i> films</a>), <a href="/wiki/Carice_van_Houten" title="Carice van Houten">Carice van Houten</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Michiel_Huisman" title="Michiel Huisman">Michiel Huisman</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Rutger_Hauer" title="Rutger Hauer">Rutger Hauer</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Jeroen_Krabb%C3%A9" title="Jeroen Krabbé">Jeroen Krabbé</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Living_Daylights" title="The Living Daylights">The Living Daylights</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Derek_de_Lint" title="Derek de Lint">Derek de Lint</a>.</p>
<p>The Netherlands has a well developed television market, with both multiple commercial and non-commercial broadcasters. Imported TV programmes, as well as interviews with responses in a foreign language, are virtually always shown with the original sound, and subtitled. The only exception are shows for children.</p>
<p>TV exports from the Netherlands mostly take the form of specific formats and franchises, most notably through internationally active TV production conglomerate <a href="/wiki/Endemol" title="Endemol">Endemol</a>, founded by Dutch <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">media</a> <a href="/wiki/Business_magnate" title="Business magnate">tycoons</a> <a href="/wiki/John_de_Mol,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="John de Mol, Jr.">John de Mol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joop_van_den_Ende" title="Joop van den Ende">Joop van den Ende</a>. Headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, Endemol has around 90 companies in over 30 countries. Endemol and its subsidiaries create and run reality, talent, and game show franchises worldwide, including <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Brother (TV series)">Big Brother</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Deal_or_No_Deal" title="Deal or No Deal">Deal or No Deal</a></i>. John de Mol later started his own company <a href="/wiki/Tien_(TV_channel)" title="Tien (TV channel)">Talpa</a> which created show franchises like <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(TV_series)" title="The Voice (TV series)"><i>The Voice</i></a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Utopia_(U.S._reality_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Utopia (U.S. reality TV series)">Utopia</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports in the Netherlands">Sports in the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NED-DEN_Euro_2012_(10).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg/220px-NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg/330px-NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg/440px-NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="656" data-file-height="593" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NED-DEN_Euro_2012_(10).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dutch star football players <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a> in a match in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Approximately 4.5 million of the 16.8 million people in the Netherlands are registered to one of the 35,000 sports clubs in the country. About two-thirds of the population between 15 and 75 participates in sports weekly.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[200]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular participant sport in the Netherlands, before <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> as the second and third most popular team sports. Tennis, gymnastics and golf are the three most widely engaged in individual sports.<sup id="cite_ref-sport_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sport-206">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>Organisation of sports began at the end of the 19th century and the beginning of the 20th century. Federations for sports were established (such as the speed skating federation in 1882), rules were unified and sports clubs came into existence. A Dutch National Olympic Committee was established in 1912. Thus far, the nation has won 266 medals at the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a> and another 110 medals at the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympic Games</a>.</p>
<p>In international competition Dutch national teams and athletes are dominant in several fields of sport. The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_women%27s_national_field_hockey_team" title="Netherlands women's national field hockey team">Netherlands women's field hockey team</a> is the most successful team in <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Hockey_World_Cup" title="Women's Hockey World Cup">World Cup</a> history. The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_baseball_team" title="Netherlands national baseball team">Netherlands baseball team</a> have won the <a href="/wiki/European_Baseball_Championship" title="European Baseball Championship">European championship</a> 20 times out of 32 events. Dutch <a href="/wiki/K-1" title="K-1">K-1</a> <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxers</a> have won the <a href="/wiki/K-1_World_Grand_Prix" title="K-1 World Grand Prix">K-1 World Grand Prix</a> 15 times out of 19 tournaments.</p>
<p>The Dutch <a href="/wiki/Speed_skating" title="Speed skating">speed skaters'</a> performance at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a>, where they won 8 out of 12 events, 23 out of 36 medals, including 4 clean sweeps, is the most dominant performance in a single sport in Olympic history.</p>
<p>Motorcycle racing at the TT Assen Circuit has a long history. Assen is the only venue to have held a round of the Motorcycle World Championship every year since its creation in 1949. The circuit was purpose built for the Dutch TT in 1954, with previous events having been held on public roads.</p>
<p>Limburger <a href="/wiki/Max_Verstappen" title="Max Verstappen">Max Verstappen</a> currently races in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_Spanish_Grand_Prix" title="2016 Spanish Grand Prix">was the first Dutchman to win a Grand Prix</a>. The coastal resort of <a href="/wiki/Circuit_Park_Zandvoort" title="Circuit Park Zandvoort">Zandvoort</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Grand_Prix" title="Dutch Grand Prix">Dutch Grand Prix</a> from 1958 to 1985.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_men%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Netherlands men's national volleyball team">Volleyball national men's team</a> has also been successful, winning the silver medal at the <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_1992_Summer_Olympics" title="Volleyball at the 1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> and the gold medal <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics" title="Volleyball at the 1996 Summer Olympics">four years later</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>. The biggest success of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_women%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Netherlands women's national volleyball team">women's national team</a> was winning the <a href="/wiki/1995_Women%27s_European_Volleyball_Championship" title="1995 Women's European Volleyball Championship">European Championship in 1995</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIVB_Volleyball_World_Grand_Prix" title="2007 FIVB Volleyball World Grand Prix">World Grand Prix in 2007</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG/220px-Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG/330px-Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG/440px-Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Simple_Dutch_meal.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An example of traditional Dutch dinner: <a href="/wiki/Brussels_sprout" title="Brussels sprout">Brussels sprouts</a>, boiled potatoes and sausage, including its gravy.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_cuisine" title="Dutch cuisine">Dutch cuisine</a></div>
<p>Originally, the country's cuisine was shaped by the practices of <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Farming" class="mw-redirect" title="Farming">farming</a>, including the cultivation of the soil for growing crops and raising domesticated animals. Dutch cuisine is simple and straightforward, and contains many dairy products. Breakfast and lunch are typically bread with toppings, with cereal for breakfast as an alternative. Traditionally, dinner consists of potatoes, a portion of meat, and (seasonal) vegetables. The Dutch diet was relatively high in carbohydrates and fat, reflecting the dietary needs of the labourers whose culture moulded the country. Without many refinements, it is best described as rustic, though many holidays are still celebrated with special foods. In the course of the twentieth century this diet changed and became much more <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">cosmopolitan</a>, with most <a href="/wiki/Global_cuisine" title="Global cuisine">global cuisines</a> being represented in the major cities.</p>
<p>Modern culinary writers distinguish between three general regional forms of Dutch cuisine. The regions in the northeast of the Netherlands, roughly the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Groningen_(province)" title="Groningen (province)">Groningen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overijssel" title="Overijssel">Overijssel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gelderland" title="Gelderland">Gelderland</a> north of the <a href="/wiki/Grote_rivieren" title="Grote rivieren">great rivers</a> are the least populated area of the Netherlands. The late (18th century) introduction of large scale agriculture means that the cuisine is generally known for its many kinds of meats. The relative lack of farms allowed for an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Game_(meat)" class="mw-redirect" title="Game (meat)">game</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">husbandry</a>, though dishes near the coastal regions of Friesland, Groningen and the parts of Overijssel bordering the <a href="/wiki/IJsselmeer" title="IJsselmeer">IJsselmeer</a> also include a large amount of fish. The various dried sausages, belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Metworst" title="Metworst">metworst</a>-family of Dutch sausages are found throughout this region and are highly prized for their often very strong taste. Also smoked sausages are common, of which (<i>Gelderse</i>) <i><a href="/wiki/Rookworst" title="Rookworst">rookworst</a></i> is the most renowned. The sausage contains a lot of fat and is very juicy. Larger sausages are often eaten alongside <i><a href="/wiki/Stamppot" title="Stamppot">stamppot</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hutspot" title="Hutspot">hutspot</a></i> or <i>zuurkool</i> (<a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">sauerkraut</a>); whereas smaller ones are often eaten as a <a href="/wiki/Street_food" title="Street food">street food</a>. The provinces are also home to hard textured <a href="/wiki/Rye_bread" title="Rye bread">rye bread</a>, pastries and cookies, the latter heavily spiced with <a href="/wiki/Ginger" title="Ginger">ginger</a> or <a href="/wiki/Succade" title="Succade">succade</a> or contain small bits of meat. Various kinds of <i>Kruidkoek</i> (such as <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groninger_koek" class="extiw" title="nl:Groninger koek">Groninger koek</a>), <i><a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fryske_d%C3%BAmkes" class="extiw" title="nl:Fryske dúmkes">Fryske dúmkes</a></i> and <i><a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/spekdik" class="extiw" title="nl:spekdik">spekdikken</a></i> (small savory pancakes cooked in a waffle iron) are considered typical. Notable characteristics of <i>Fries roggebrood</i> (Frisian rye bread) is its long baking time (up to 20 hours), resulting in a sweet taste and a deep dark colour.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[202]</a></sup> In terms of alcoholic beverages, the region is renowned for its many <a href="/wiki/Bitters" title="Bitters">bitters</a> (such as <i><a href="/wiki/Beerenburg" title="Beerenburg">Beerenburg</a></i>) and other high-proof liquors rather than beer, which is, apart from <i><a href="/wiki/Jenever" title="Jenever">Jenever</a></i>, typical for the rest of the country. As a coastal region, Friesland is home to low-lying grasslands, and thus has a cheese production in common with the Western cuisine. <i>Friese Nagelkaas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Friesian_Clove" title="Friesian Clove">Friesian Clove</a>) is a notable example.</p>
<p>The provinces of <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(province)" title="Utrecht (province)">Utrecht</a> and the Gelderlandic region of <a href="/wiki/Betuwe" title="Betuwe">Betuwe</a> are the parts of the Netherlands which make up the region in which western Dutch cuisine is found. Because of the abundance of water and flat grass lands that are found here, the area is known for its many dairy products, which includes prominent cheeses such as <a href="/wiki/Gouda_(cheese)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gouda (cheese)">Gouda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leyden_cheese" title="Leyden cheese">Leyden</a> (spiced cheese with cumin), <a href="/wiki/Edam_(cheese)" class="mw-redirect" title="Edam (cheese)">Edam</a> (traditionally in small spheres) as well as <a href="/wiki/Leerdammer" title="Leerdammer">Leerdammer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beemster_Cheese" class="mw-redirect" title="Beemster Cheese">Beemster</a>, while the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Zaanstreek" class="mw-redirect" title="Zaanstreek">Zaanstreek</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a> is since the 16th century known for its <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">mayonnaise</a>, typical whole-grain <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">mustards</a><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[203]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a> industry. Zeeland and South Holland produce a lot of butter, which contains a larger amount of <a href="/wiki/Milkfat" class="mw-redirect" title="Milkfat">milkfat</a> than most other European butter varieties. A by-product of the butter-making process, <i>karnemelk</i> (<a href="/wiki/Buttermilk" title="Buttermilk">buttermilk</a>), is also considered typical for this region. <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">Seafood</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Soused_herring" title="Soused herring">soused herring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_mussel" title="Blue mussel">mussels</a> (called <i>Zeeuwse Mossels</i>, since all Dutch mussels for consumption are cleaned in Zeeland's <a href="/wiki/Oosterschelde" class="mw-redirect" title="Oosterschelde">Oosterschelde</a>), <a href="/wiki/European_eel" title="European eel">eels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimps</a> are widely available and typical for the region. <i><a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kibbeling" class="extiw" title="nl:Kibbeling">Kibbeling</a></i>, once a local delicacy consisting of small chunks of battered <a href="/wiki/Whitefish_(fisheries_term)" title="Whitefish (fisheries term)">white fish</a>, has become a national <a href="/wiki/Fast_food" title="Fast food">fast food</a>, just as <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lekkerbekje" class="extiw" title="nl:Lekkerbekje">lekkerbek</a>. Pastries in this area tend to be quite doughy, and often contain large amounts of sugar; either caramelised, powdered or crystallised. The <i><a href="/wiki/Oliebol" title="Oliebol">oliebol</a></i> (in its modern form) and <i><a href="/wiki/Zeeuwse_bolus" title="Zeeuwse bolus">Zeeuwse bolus</a></i> are good examples. Cookies are also produced in great number and tend to contain a lot of butter and sugar, like <i><a href="/wiki/Stroopwafel" title="Stroopwafel">stroopwafel</a></i>, as well as a filling of some kind, mostly almond, like <i><a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gevulde_koek" class="extiw" title="nl:Gevulde koek">gevulde koek</a></i>. The traditional alcoholic beverages of this region are <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> (strong pale lager) and <i><a href="/wiki/Jenever" title="Jenever">Jenever</a></i>, a high proof <a href="/wiki/Juniper" title="Juniper">juniper</a>-flavored spirit, that came to be known in England as <a href="/wiki/Gin" title="Gin">gin</a>. A noted exception within the traditional Dutch alcoholic landscape, <i><a href="/wiki/Advocaat" title="Advocaat">Advocaat</a></i>, a rich and creamy liqueur made from eggs, sugar and brandy, is also native to this region.</p>
<p>The Southern Dutch cuisine consists of the cuisines of the Dutch provinces of <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. It is renowned for its many rich pastries, soups, stews and vegetable dishes and is often called Burgundian which is a Dutch idiom invoking the rich Burgundian court which ruled the Low Countries in the Middle Ages, renowned for its splendor and great feasts. It is the only Dutch culinary region that developed an <a href="/wiki/Haute_cuisine" title="Haute cuisine">haute cuisine</a>. Pastries are abundant, often with rich fillings of cream, custard or fruits. Cakes, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Vlaai" title="Vlaai">Vlaai</a></i> from Limburg and the <i>Moorkop</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bossche_Bol" class="mw-redirect" title="Bossche Bol">Bossche Bol</a></i> from Brabant, are typical pastries. Savoury pastries also occur, with the <i>worstenbroodje</i> (a roll with a sausage of <a href="/wiki/Ground_beef" title="Ground beef">ground beef</a>, literally translates into sausage bread) being the most popular. The traditional alcoholic beverage of the region is beer. There are many local brands, ranging from <i><a href="/wiki/Trappist_beer" title="Trappist beer">Trappist</a></i> to <i><a href="/wiki/Kriek_lambic" title="Kriek lambic">Kriek</a></i>. 5 of the 10 <i>International Trappist Association</i> recognised breweries in the world, are located in the Southern Dutch cultural area. Beer, like wine in French cuisine, is also used in cooking; often in stews.</p>
<p>In early 2014, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> ranked the Netherlands as the country with the most nutritious, plentiful and healthy food, in a comparison of 125 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[205]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_heritage">Colonial heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Colonial heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indos_in_the_Dutch_East_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Indos in the Dutch East Indies">Indos in the Dutch East Indies</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg/220px-GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg/330px-GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg/440px-GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7276" data-file-height="4964" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> as it appeared in 1664. Under British rule it became known as <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the exploitations of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> in the 17th century, to the <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">colonisations</a> in the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch imperial possessions</a> continued to expand, reaching their greatest extent by establishing a hegemony of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> in the early 20th century. The Dutch East Indies, which later formed modern-day Indonesia, was one of the most valuable European colonies in the world and the most important one for the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[206]</a></sup> Over 350 years of mutual heritage has left a significant cultural mark on the Netherlands.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a> of the 17th century, the Netherlands urbanised considerably, mostly financed by corporate revenue from the Asian trade monopolies. Social status was based on merchants' income, which reduced <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a> and considerably changed the dynamics of Dutch society. When the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Royal Family">Dutch Royal Family</a> was established in 1815, much of its wealth came from Colonial trade.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>Universities such as the Royal <a href="/wiki/Leiden_University" title="Leiden University">Leiden University</a>, founded in the 16th century, have developed into leading knowledge centres for <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian</a> and Indonesian studies.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[208]</a></sup> Leiden University has produced leading academics such as <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Snouck_Hurgronje" title="Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje">Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje</a>, and still has academics who specialise in Indonesian languages and cultures. Leiden University and in particular <a href="/wiki/KITLV" class="mw-redirect" title="KITLV">KITLV</a> are educational and scientific institutions that to this day share both an intellectual and historical interest in Indonesian studies. Other scientific institutions in the Netherlands include the Amsterdam <a href="/wiki/Tropenmuseum" title="Tropenmuseum">Tropenmuseum</a>, an anthropological museum with massive collections of Indonesian art, culture, ethnography and anthropology.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg" width="220" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg 2x" data-file-width="638" data-file-height="700" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A European doctor vaccinates <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Indonesian people">Indonesian</a> patients</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_East_Indies_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Dutch East Indies Army">Royal Dutch East Indies Army</a> (KNIL) are maintained by the <a href="/wiki/Regiment_Van_Heutsz" class="mw-redirect" title="Regiment Van Heutsz">Regiment Van Heutsz</a> of the modern <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Army" title="Royal Netherlands Army">Royal Netherlands Army</a>. A dedicated <i><a href="/wiki/Bronbeek" title="Bronbeek">Bronbeek</a> Museum</i>, a former home for retired KNIL soldiers, exists in <a href="/wiki/Arnhem" title="Arnhem">Arnhem</a> to this day.</p>
<p>A specific segment of Dutch literature called <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Indies_literature" title="Dutch Indies literature">Dutch Indies literature</a> still exists and includes established authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Louis_Couperus" title="Louis Couperus">Louis Couperus</a>, the writer of "The Hidden Force", taking the colonial era as an important source of inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[209]</a></sup> One of the great masterpieces of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch literature">Dutch literature</a> is the book "<a href="/wiki/Max_Havelaar" title="Max Havelaar">Max Havelaar</a>", written by <a href="/wiki/Multatuli" title="Multatuli">Multatuli</a> in 1860.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[210]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of Dutchmen that repatriated to the Netherlands after and during the Indonesian revolution are <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Indo</a> (Eurasian), native to the islands of the Dutch East Indies. This relatively large Eurasian population had developed over a period of 400 years and were classified by colonial law as belonging to the European legal community.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[211]</a></sup> In Dutch they are referred to as <i>Indische Nederlanders</i> or as Indo (short for Indo-European).<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>Including their second generation descendants, Indos are currently the largest foreign-born group in the Netherlands. In 2008, the Dutch Census Bureau for Statistics (CBS)<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[213]</a></sup> registered 387,000 first- and second-generation Indos living in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[214]</a></sup> Although considered fully assimilated into Dutch society, as the main ethnic minority in the Netherlands, these 'repatriants' have played a pivotal role in introducing elements of Indonesian culture into Dutch mainstream culture.</p>
<p>Practically every town in the Netherlands has a "Toko" (Dutch Indonesian Shop) or an Indonesian restaurant<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[215]</a></sup> and many '<a href="/wiki/Pasar_Malam" class="mw-redirect" title="Pasar Malam">Pasar Malam</a>' (Night market in Malay/Indonesian) fairs are organised throughout the year. Many Indonesian dishes and foodstuffs have become commonplace in the Netherlands. <a href="/wiki/Rijsttafel" title="Rijsttafel">Rijsttafel</a>, a colonial culinary concept, and dishes such as <a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">Nasi goreng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">satay</a> are very popular in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[216]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-168"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-168">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The religious development of the Netherlands in the 20th century, and its three defining censuses: The census of 31 December 1930 recorded various Protestants at 46.3%, Roman Catholics at 36.5% and the remainder at 17.2%. The census of 31 May 1947 recorded various Protestants at 42.3%, Roman Catholics at 38.6% and the remainder at 19.1%. The census of 31 May 1960 recorded various Protestants at 40.7%, Roman Catholics at 40.5% and the remainder at 18.8%.</span></li>

<dl>
<dt>Geography and environment</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Burke, Gerald L. <i>The making of Dutch towns: A study in urban development from the 10th–17th centuries</i> (1960)</li>
<li>Lambert, Audrey M. <i>The Making of the Dutch Landscape: An Historical Geography of the Netherlands</i> (1985); focus on the history of land reclamation</li>
<li>Meijer, Henk. <i>Compact geography of the Netherlands</i> (1985)</li>
<li>Riley, R. C., and G. J. Ashworth. <i>Benelux: An Economic Geography of Belgium, the Netherlands, and Luxembourg</i> (1975) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.questia.com/read/85882918/benelux-an-economic-geography-of-belgium-the-netherlands">online</a></li>
</ul>

<div>
<ul>
<li><sup><small>3</small></sup> <span class="wrap">Became <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands#Countries" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">constituent countries</a> of the Kingdom of the Netherlands; <a href="/wiki/Suriname_(Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Suriname (Kingdom of the Netherlands)">Suriname</a> gained <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">full independence</a> in 1975, Curaçao and Dependencies was renamed to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>, which was eventually dissolved in 2010.</span></li>
</ul>
